Phase 4 ISC-P4-REPO-1 owns end-to-end repo-URL openability verification; the same forward-coupling pattern as EditPageLink/SG-16, NavBar/SG-14, Breadcrumbs/SG-15, index.astro CTAs/SG-21).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **The `<nav>`-as-print-hide guardrail from iter-17 cuts both ways — it also tells you when *not* to print-hide.** Iter-17's reflection (1) clarified that print-hiding is for editor chrome, not for content. SG-17 took that one step further: VersionFooter is metadata about the document itself (version, amendment date, source-of-record link), so it belongs in the printed archival copy — the version stamp IS the doctrinal claim that "this is version X as of date Y." Printing a canonical document without its version stamp would be like printing a contract without its signature date. Lesson: when iter-N's reflection establishes a categorization (chrome vs nav vs content), iter-N+1 should ask whether the same categorization disambiguates a different choice. Here, "is this chrome or content?" disambiguated "should this be print-hidden?" — VersionFooter is content. (2) **One prop normalization pattern, two consumers — codify before a third arrives.** EditPageLink (SG-16) introduced `sourcePath.replace(/^\/+/, "")`. VersionFooter (SG-17) repeated it verbatim. Both compose URLs of the form `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/<verb>/main/${sourcePath}`. When SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro lands and starts passing `entry.id` (Astro v5 leading-slash-free convention) to both `<EditPageLink>` and `<VersionFooter>`, the regex becomes operationally a no-op for the common case and a defense against accidental leading slashes for edge cases. The rule-of-three for extraction has not been reached (only two callers, both passing what is effectively the same value), so no helper function yet — but it's now worth noting in DECISIONS.md if a third repo-URL-composing component appears, the right move is to extract `function repoUrlFor(verb: 'edit' | 'blob' | 'commits', sourcePath: string): string` in `src/lib/repo.ts` and consume from all three sites. Forward-pointers from iter-18: (a) SG-18 TableOfContents.astro continues the default sequence; it does not consume `SOURCE_REPO_URL`, so the rule-of-three above remains at two consumers; (b) SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro is the integration site for both VersionFooter and TableOfContents — when it lands, the `sourcePath` it passes to `<VersionFooter>` should come from `entry.filePath` or `entry.id` per the Astro v5 content-collection API; (c) when DECISION-REPO resolves, both EditPageLink's `/edit/main/` segment and VersionFooter's `/blob/main/` and `/commits/main/` segments need to be re-checked against the chosen platform's URL grammar — GitHub uses `/edit/<branch>/`, `/blob/<branch>/`, `/commits/<branch>/`; Forgejo uses `/_edit/<branch>/`, `/src/branch/<branch>/`, `/commits/branch/<branch>/`. A platform switch is a non-trivial edit across at least these two files and ideally the extracted `repoUrlFor` helper noted above.
- **Remaining:** 8 Phase 0 milestones pending (32 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 31 + ISC-FND-CMP-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **Case-sensitive invariant greps are a verification-liability when the asserted text and the implementation diverge in casing.** Iter-19's first attempt at INV-NAV-1's grep returned 0 matches against NavBar.astro and briefly looked like a real regression — but NavBar uses uppercase labels (`CREED`, `CODEX`, …) as a CRT-aesthetic convention, while `docs/invariant_requirements.md:151` lists them in title case ("Creed, Codex, Practices…"). The text content renders identically (browsers do not normalize), the doctrinal requirement (six entries in IA §4 order, no extras) is met, and the case-insensitive re-run confirmed PASS. Lesson for SG-24 `tests/invariants.spec.ts`: NavBar-presence-and-order assertions should be case-insensitive (the invariant is *which entries appear in what order*, not the literal casing of the source) AND should require ALL six labels in order, not just any. A future invariant could codify casing if that becomes load-bearing, but it is not load-bearing today. (2) **The TOC integration with SG-19 has a correct-by-construction guarantee worth preserving in the CanonicalDoc wiring.** Because the heading list (rendered into the page) and the TOC link list both come from the same `MarkdownHeading[]` returned by Astro's content-collection `render()` call, the `#${slug}` fragments cannot drift from the heading `id`s. When SG-19 lands, the wiring should pass `entry.headings` directly to `<TableOfContents>` without intermediate transformation — any transform (re-slugging, filtering by section, depth-clipping above what's already in this component) introduces a divergence opportunity that the build-time link checker (SG-26) would catch only after the fact. This is a strictly stronger guarantee than the build-time link checker SG-26 will provide for cross-page links, and is worth a one-line comment in CanonicalDoc.astro when written. Forward-pointers from iter-19: (a) SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro consumes both VersionFooter (SG-17) and TableOfContents (this iteration), so it is the natural integration boundary — pass `entry.headings` to `<TableOfContents>` and `entry.id` (Astro v5 leading-slash-free) plus `entry.data.{version,amendedAt,firstPublishedAt}` to `<VersionFooter>`; (b) iter-18 reflection (2)'s `repoUrlFor` extraction trigger remains at two consumers (EditPageLink + VersionFooter); TableOfContents introduces no third consumer; (c) the inline IntersectionObserver pattern in TableOfContents.astro:29-58 is the first inline `<script>` in a Phase 0 component — if subsequent components need similar progressive-enhancement JS (e.g., a future copy-to-clipboard for canonical text, or a print-friendly toggle), DECISIONS.md should record whether to keep them inline per-component (locality, no bundling overhead) or extract to `src/scripts/` (reuse, hoisting, but adds an import indirection). For one occurrence, inline is correct; for three or more, extract.
- **Remaining:** 7 Phase 0 milestones pending (33 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 32 + ISC-FND-CMP-5) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

BLOCKED — INV-BUILD-2 (`pnpm astro check` requires `@astrojs/check`, not installed; SG-22 owns; no regression from iter-14..19 baseline; CanonicalDoc.astro will be exercised end-to-end by astro check only when consuming Phase 1 pages land and `@astrojs/check` is installed). PARTIAL-CONTRIBUTION — INV-NAV-2 (CanonicalDoc.astro emits no new `<a href="/...">` literals; internal nav flows through Breadcrumbs/Footer/NavBar — existing components. External source/revision-history anchors via VersionFooter resolve through the `SOURCE_REPO_URL` placeholder `https://github.com/PLACEHOLDER/technodruid` per DECISION-REPO; Phase 4 ISC-P4-REPO-1 + ISC-P4-EDIT-1 own end-to-end openability verification post-DECISION-REPO resolution. TOC in-page `#${slug}` anchors are correct-by-construction per iter-19 reflection (2) — same `MarkdownHeading[]` populates both the rendered headings and the TOC link list, so they cannot drift). Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-LAY-1 (seven-point sub-check against PRD line 238 spec: (1) `entry: CollectionEntry<"canonical">` accepted — CanonicalDoc.astro:11 typed in Props interface, :15 destructured from Astro.props; (2) `<Breadcrumbs>` rendered — line 22; (3) `<CanonicalBadge>` rendered — line 24 (wrapped in `<div class="mt-4">` for layout spacing without inline-style); (4) `<h1>` from title — line 26 `<h1>{title}</h1>` derives from `entry.data.title` destructured at line 16; (5) sticky `<TableOfContents>` derived from `<h2>` and `<h3>` in slot — line 29 `<TableOfContents headings={headings} />` passes the `MarkdownHeading[]` directly; TableOfContents.astro:14 wraps in `<nav class="sticky top-4 text-sm">` (sticky satisfied), TableOfContents.astro:9 filters `depth <= 3` (so `<h2>` and `<h3>` are the heading depths surfaced); (6) slotted MDX content — line 32 `<slot />` accepts whatever Content the consuming page renders; (7) `<VersionFooter>` with version + amendedAt + firstPublishedAt + source-repo + revision-history — lines 33-38 pass all four data props; sourcePath construction at line 17 feeds VersionFooter.astro:14-15 which produce both repo links — five-field contract met).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **Extending a load-bearing root layout safely means making the default a no-op.** Base.astro is consumed by every page in the site, today and forever, so any prop addition must not change the rendered HTML for existing callers. The chosen pattern — `["flex", "items-center", bodyClass].filter(Boolean).join(" ")` with `bodyClass?: string` defaulting to `undefined` — is bit-identical for existing index.astro (the filter drops the undefined, producing exactly `"flex items-center"`). Verification: dist/index.html before and after this iteration should differ by zero bytes inside the `<body>` tag. The lesson generalizes: when adding an optional prop to a shared root, the falsy/undefined path must produce exactly the prior output. A naive implementation like `<body class={\`flex items-center ${bodyClass ?? ""}\`}>` would introduce a trailing space — visually invisible but bit-different — and a brittle test could regress on it. The `filter(Boolean).join(" ")` idiom is the safer composition. Worth codifying in DECISIONS.md if a third layout extends Base with a similar opt-in class — at that point an `assembleBodyClasses(...parts: (string | undefined)[]): string` helper in `src/lib/css.ts` may earn its keep. (2) **`entry.filePath` is the correct sourcePath provenance in Astro v5, but the fallback chain matters.** Astro v5's content-collection entry exposes `filePath` as a string like `"./src/content/canonical/codex.md"` (per Astro v5 docs); my implementation defensively chains `entry.filePath ?? "src/content/canonical/${entry.id}"` with a `.replace(/^\.\//, "")` to strip the leading `./` that Astro adds. This handles three failure modes simultaneously: (a) Astro v5 surface drift where `filePath` becomes optional — fallback to `entry.id`; (b) accidental Astro internals that strip `filePath` — same fallback; (c) the standard case where `filePath` is the documented `"./src/..."` — strip the `./` so the joined URL never produces `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/blob/main/./src/...`. The chain is three lines of defensive logic that buy resilience across a real Astro version change. Forward-pointers from iter-20: (a) SG-20 LivingDoc.astro should mirror this pattern — accept `entry: CollectionEntry<"living">`, compute sourcePath the same way for EditPageLink, but living entries also need lastEditedAt + contributors which come from `entry.data` (lastEditedAt, contributors) per content.config.ts:21-24; (b) SG-21 index.astro was already pulled forward in iter-15; SG-19's CanonicalDoc landing now enables Phase 1 ISC-MVP-4 (codex page) to start using `<CanonicalDoc entry={entry} headings={headings}><Content /></CanonicalDoc>` once a canonical entry exists; (c) the rule-of-three for `repoUrlFor` extraction remains at two consumers (EditPageLink + VersionFooter) — CanonicalDoc composes through VersionFooter rather than introducing a third direct composer, so the helper is still deferred; SG-20 LivingDoc will also compose through EditPageLink rather than directly, preserving the two-consumer count; (d) iter-19 reflection (1)'s case-insensitive grep convention applied successfully this iteration without any false-negative scare — the convention should become permanent in SG-24 invariants.spec.ts; (e) the optional-prop-default-no-op pattern from reflection (1) should be invoked verbatim when SG-22 lands and the `verify` script chain runs — any future Base.astro prop addition (e.g., `noindex?: boolean` for `/about/contact` if it ever needs robot exclusion) should be code-reviewed against the bit-identical-when-default heuristic.
- **Remaining:** 6 Phase 0 milestones pending (34 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 33 + ISC-FND-LAY-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-LAY-2 (eight-point sub-check against PRD line 239 spec: (1) `entry: CollectionEntry<"living">` accepted — LivingDoc.astro:10 typed in Props interface, :13 destructured from Astro.props; (2) `<Breadcrumbs>` rendered — line 21; (3) `<LivingBadge>` rendered — line 23 (wrapped in `<div class="mt-4">` for spacing without inline-style); (4) `<h1>` from title — line 25 `<h1>{title}</h1>`; (5) slotted MDX content — line 26 `<slot />`; (6) `<LastEditedStamp>` — line 28 receives `date={lastEditedAt}` destructured from `entry.data` at line 14; (7) contributor list — line 29 `<p>Contributors: {contributorList}</p>`; `contributorList` computed at line 16 from `entry.data.contributors` (string[], default [] per content.config.ts:23) with empty-array fallback to "—"; (8) `<EditPageLink>` resolving to entry's source path — line 31 receives sourcePath computed at line 15 with three-tier provenance: `entry.data.sourcePath` (schema-declared optional override per content.config.ts:24) → `entry.filePath` (Astro v5 documented field) → `"src/content/living/${entry.id}"` (constructed fallback); `.replace(/^\.\//, "")` strips Astro's documented `./` prefix so the joined URL never produces `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/edit/main/./src/...`).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **An optional schema field becomes a deliberate override only when the layout's provenance chain prefers it over the structural default.** The living schema's `sourcePath: z.string().optional()` field would be dead weight if the layout used `entry.filePath` unconditionally. The three-tier chain `entry.data.sourcePath ?? entry.filePath ?? constructed-fallback` gives the schema field a real purpose — an author who needs to point "Edit this page" at a different repo path (e.g., living content sourced from a Wiki module, a fork, or an alternate branch) can set it via frontmatter without touching the layout. CanonicalDoc deliberately omits this tier because canonical content has no equivalent schema override (canonical schema lists no `sourcePath`). The lesson: don't shrug at "optional" schema fields — either delete them (if no layout consumes them) or wire them through the provenance chain (if they're meant to override defaults). Forward-pointer for SG-6 caretaker: if `living.sourcePath` is never used in practice, it should be removed in a content-config cleanup pass; the cost of carrying an unused optional field is documentation drift, not bytes. (2) **Invariant-by-fallback is stronger than invariant-by-discipline when the schema allows the failure mode.** INV-LIV-1 mandates "contributor list (may be a single entry)." The schema permits `contributors: []` via `.default([])`. If the layout renders nothing when the array is empty, the invariant fails for entries that ship with an empty contributors list — and the failure is a content bug, surfaced only by tests against actual pages. The `contributors.length > 0 ? contributors.join(", ") : "—"` fallback at line 16 shifts the guarantee from author discipline (must remember to add contributors) to layout structural enforcement (the "Contributors:" line is always present, even if its value is the em-dash placeholder). The trade-off: an "empty contributors" page now reads "Contributors: —" instead of being structurally invalid — visible to the reader as a marker that the field exists but is unfilled. For a doctrinally-archival site, visible-absent is better than silently-absent. Forward-pointers from iter-21: (a) SG-20 closes the layout-component layer (Base + CanonicalDoc + LivingDoc) — Phase 0 milestones remaining are testing infrastructure (SG-22 package.json deps + scripts, SG-23 playwright config, SG-24 invariants spec, SG-25 a11y spec, SG-26 build spec); (b) the natural next subgoal is SG-22 (package.json), because it unblocks `pnpm astro check` (INV-BUILD-2), `pnpm test` (SG-23..26), and the `verify` script chain — every subsequent test subgoal depends on it; (c) iter-10 forward-pointer for SG-22 still live: DECIDE whether `verify` runs greenfield (asserts full chain passes) or progressively (scripts exist, baseline failures accepted); given INV-BUILD-1 PASS for 7 consecutive iterations (iter-15..21) and no canonical/living pages yet, greenfield is now achievable for the check + build halves but not test:ci (no tests exist yet — chicken-and-egg); the resolution is staged: install deps + add scripts in SG-22, accept that `test:ci` will exit non-zero until SG-23/24 exist, then re-verify after each test file lands; (d) iter-19 reflection (1) case-insensitive invariant grep convention has held for two iterations (iter-20, iter-21) — codify in SG-24 invariants.spec.ts when written; (e) the `repoUrlFor` rule-of-three remains at two consumers (EditPageLink, VersionFooter); LivingDoc composes through EditPageLink rather than introducing a third direct composer — pattern from iter-20 reflection (1) preserved; first real third-consumer trigger likely lands in Phase 2 (e.g., wheel-events RSS feed item permalinks referencing repo paths, ISC-P2-6).
- **Remaining:** 5 Phase 0 milestones pending (35 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 34 + ISC-FND-LAY-2) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Reflection:** Three observations. (1) **A 4-iteration BLOCKED invariant is not a stall — it's a deferred dependency.** INV-BUILD-2 was BLOCKED for iter-18/19/20/21 because `@astrojs/check` was not installed; the loop kept marking it BLOCKED rather than treating BLOCKED as FAIL. This is a deliberate design feature: invariants whose toolchain isn't installed yet cannot regress the iteration, and the right resolution is to land the unlock subgoal (here, SG-22) before any subgoal that would re-encounter the missing toolchain. The lesson: when classifying an invariant as BLOCKED, the loop owes a forward-pointer to the unblocking subgoal — and that subgoal's pre-flight must include the unblocked invariant explicitly so the unblocking is verified, not implied. SG-22's pre-flight did this for INV-BUILD-2: PASS with explicit BLOCKED→PASS transition evidence. (2) **Script EXISTENCE vs script PASSING is a contract distinction worth honoring.** PRD line 213 says `package.json includes ... scripts test, test:ci, check, verify (where verify chains check → build → test:ci)`. It does NOT say `pnpm verify exits 0`. Iter-22 honored the literal contract: scripts exist and chain correctly (verified via `jq '.scripts.verify | test("check[^&]*&&[^&]*build[^&]*&&[^&]*test:ci")'` → true), but `pnpm verify` itself was not executed because `test:ci` would exit non-zero pre-SG-23/24 (no Playwright tests yet — chicken-and-egg). The staged-resolution from iter-21 forward-pointer (c) was applied: install + wire in SG-22, accept `test:ci` non-zero, re-verify after SG-23/24/25/26 land. Without this distinction, SG-22 would be unsolvable without merging in SG-23/24 — violating the loop's "one iteration unit per iteration" rule. Forward-pointer: when SG-26 lands the last test file, run `pnpm verify` end-to-end and capture EXIT=0 as the proof-of-chain evidence; that becomes the first true greenfield verify pass. (3) **`pnpm add -D` is the correct tool for SG-22 — not direct package.json edits — because lockfile atomicity matters.** Editing `package.json`'s `devDependencies` and then running `pnpm install` is a two-step that can leave `pnpm-lock.yaml` momentarily inconsistent if the install fails (e.g., network blip, registry rate limit). `pnpm add -D pkg1 pkg2 pkg3` atomically writes both files. The "Ignored build scripts: esbuild, sharp" warning is benign — those are postinstall opt-ins (pnpm 10+ security feature), and the 8-iter INV-BUILD-1 green streak proves the binaries already work from prior approval. Recommendation for future infra subgoals: prefer `pnpm add -D` over manual JSON edits for any dependency change. Forward-pointers from iter-22: (a) **new SG-27 (cleanup) candidate** — delete `src/components/HeroImage.astro` (orphan, INV-CODE-2 violator) AND `src/assets/blog-fallback.jpg` (orphan from SG-11 forward-pointer); single trivial iteration closes two carryovers; ORIENT step 4b should add this in iter-23 if no PRD changes intervene. ### Iteration 23 — 2026-05-17
- **Start commit:** `696bd88`
- **Artifacts:** `src/pages/index.astro` (modify — creed spacing + text-left + bottom CTA justify-between) + `src/components/NavBar.astro` (modify — lg-scoped column constraint + justify-between) (tier: standard)
- **Subgoal:** SG-21b (new this iter, split from completed SG-21 per ORIENT 4b — new ISC-FND-IDX-2 added by user mid-PRD between iter-22 and iter-23). SG-21b's scope grew through four mid-iteration ISC amendments: (1) spacing; (2) left-justified; (3) bottom CTA edge alignment; (4) top NavBar edge alignment (the actual final concern). Verified via Playwright MCP screenshots + browser_evaluate bounding-box JS — first iteration in this PRD to use real visual verification.
- **Milestones addressed:** ISC-FND-IDX-2 (PASS — four-point sub-check via Playwright at viewport 1280×900: section.left=256 / section.right=1024; CREED.left=256 / ABOUT.right=1024 (top NavBar); bottom-CTA first.left=256 / last.right=1024; creed glyph-left=256 for all 6 lines; space-y-10 = 40px between adjacent <li> exceeds wrapping gap of 19-24px).
- **Invariants verified:** Direct PASS — INV-DOC-1 (`grep -rcE 'fonts\.(googleapis|gstatic)\.com|use\.typekit\.net|fonts\.cdnfonts\.com|fast\.fonts\.net' dist/` → TOTAL:0); INV-DOC-2 (TOTAL:0 in dist/; plausible.io exception preserved); INV-DOC-3 (TOTAL:0 in src/+public/); INV-DOC-5 (TOTAL:0 in dist/); INV-LIC-1 (`grep -cE 'rel="license"' dist/index.html` → 1); INV-LIC-2 (LICENSE + LICENSE-CONTENT both exist at repo root); INV-BUILD-1 (`pnpm build` EXIT=0 across three ACT rounds — initial spacing, text-left+nav-edges, NavBar fix; stderr empty all three; baseline 5 [WARN] [glob-loader] lines on stdout; 9-iter green-build streak iter-15..23); INV-BUILD-2 (`pnpm check` EXIT=0 across all three rounds; report `Result (25 files): - 0 errors - 0 warnings - 0 hints`; second consecutive PASS since iter-22 unblock); INV-BUILD-3 (dist/sitemap-index.xml present each build); INV-CODE-1 (`grep -rcE 'style="(color|font-family|background|margin|padding):' src/` → TOTAL:0; all Tailwind utility classes); INV-CODE-3 (`grep -rlE 'defineCollection|z\.object\(' src/` → only src/content.config.ts); INV-NAV-1 (six IA §4 entries preserved at NavBar.astro:9-16; only the wrapper-div class at line 21 changed; Playwright confirmed left-to-right order CREED CODEX PRACTICES GROVES LIBRARY ABOUT); INT-PROC-1 (build + check EXIT=0). PASS-NO-REGRESSION — INV-DOC-4 (Plausible surface unchanged; no <script> added); INV-A11Y-2 (`<title>Technodruid</title>` non-empty); INV-A11Y-3 (1 `<h1>` in dist/index.html, sr-only "The Creed" preserved); INV-A11Y-4 (global.css:179 @media print unchanged); INV-NAV-3 (`grep -c 'rel="license"' dist/index.html` → 1; `awk '/<footer/,/<\/footer>/' | grep -cE '©|&copy;|&#169;'` → 0). PASS-WITH-CARRYOVER — INV-CODE-2 (iter-23 contributions: `grep -cE ': any\b|<any>|as any' src/pages/index.astro src/components/NavBar.astro` → 0; global state unchanged: 1 pre-existing match at src/components/HeroImage.astro:5; carryover from iter-15 still queued for SG-27 cleanup). N/A-SCOPE — INV-CAN-1/2/3 (no canonical pages); INV-LIV-1/2 (no living pages); INV-DOC-NAME (no JSDoc added; index.astro + NavBar.astro identifiers fully derivable from name+type). DEFERRED — INV-A11Y-1 (@axe-core/playwright installed but harness not wired; SG-25 owns; iter-23 changes are class-attribute mutations only, no axe-flagging structural patterns). PARTIAL — INV-NAV-2 (zero new internal-link literals; existing CTA hrefs `/codex`, `/groves/directory`, `/practices` and NavBar hrefs `/`, `/codex`, `/practices`, `/groves`, `/library`, `/about` all unchanged).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Three observations. (1) **Visual verification with Playwright MCP changes what "evidence" means for layout ISCs.** The first three rounds of this iteration (spacing, text-left, bottom CTA justify-between) all passed the textual class-attribute checks but did not satisfy the user's actual intent — which was about the top site NavBar's CREED/ABOUT alignment, not the bottom CTA row. The textual evidence (`grep dist/index.html` for class attributes) couldn't reveal this misalignment because the misalignment was on a different element (NavBar) at a different layer (Header in Base.astro). Only the Playwright screenshot — and the magenta guide-line overlay anchored to `section.getBoundingClientRect()` — made the misalignment unambiguous within seconds. The lesson: for any ISC that describes visual alignment, layout, spacing, or positioning, the verification protocol should include a Playwright MCP screenshot at the relevant breakpoint plus bounding-box evaluation against named reference elements. Mechanical class-attribute checks are necessary but not sufficient. Forward-pointer: SG-25 (`tests/a11y.spec.ts`) and SG-26 (`tests/build.spec.ts`) should add a layout-assertions spec that captures key alignment relationships (NavBar items snap to section column edges at lg+; bottom CTA row spans column at md+; creed text starts at column-left) as Playwright invariants so regressions are caught automatically. (2) **A user-added ISC can be amended four times mid-iteration without becoming a stall.** stall_count remained 0 because each amendment refined the same underlying intent ("the index page's nav and creed should align doctrinally"), and each ACT round produced a strict superset of the previous correct state — never a regression. The protocol's stall_count is meant to fire when the same approach fails repeatedly; here, each ACT round was a DIFFERENT approach addressing a NEWLY-revealed sub-requirement. Forward-pointer: the loop's stall_count semantics should be refined in the protocol — "stall" = same approach failing on the same requirement vs "iterative refinement" = different approaches revealed by progressive user clarification. Iter-23 is the latter and should not increment stall_count. (3) **The "specification through Playwright" pattern outperforms "specification through prose."** The four-amendment trajectory began with prose ("creed should have enough space between lines to accommodate normal text wrapping"). Each amendment added more prose. The user's final clarification was a SCREENSHOT with a circled element — and that one image conveyed more precise intent than any prose phrasing could. Conclusion for future iterations: when working on visual/layout ISCs, ask the user to attach an annotated screenshot of the current state with arrows / circles pointing at the misaligned element BEFORE proposing fixes. This bypasses the prose-ambiguity → speculate → screenshot → re-speculate cycle that consumed three of this iteration's four ACT rounds. Forward-pointers from iter-23: (a) **Next iteration (24) reverts to default SG-23 (`tests/playwright.config.ts`)** since SG-21b is now complete; the testing infrastructure chain (SG-23 → SG-24 → SG-25 → SG-26) remains the natural sequence; (b) **SG-27 (cleanup) still queued** — delete HeroImage.astro + blog-fallback.jpg to close INV-CODE-2 carryover (one trivial iteration); (c) **Playwright MCP browser tools** proved invaluable for this iter — the team should pre-load `mcp__plugin_playwright_playwright__browser_*` tools earlier in any layout-touching subgoal; (d) **annotated screenshots as ISC artifacts**: the three screenshots (iter23-md-1280.png, iter23-md-1280-guides.png, iter23-md-1280-navfix.png) are kept in repo root as visual provenance for iter-23; SG-26 build spec could codify a screenshot-diff regression suite.

### Iteration 0 — 2026-05-16
- **Start commit:** `696bd88`
- **Artifacts:** `LICENSE` (create), `UNLICENSE.md` (delete), `LICENSE-CONTENT` (create) (tier: trivial)
- **Subgoal:** SG-1 — Phase 0 license files
- **Milestones addressed:** ISC-FND-LIC-1 (PASS)
- **Invariants verified:** all PASS — INV-DOC-1/2/5 positively verified against new artifacts (0 forbidden-host matches); INV-LIC-2 partial-pass (LICENSE-CONTENT exists with CC BY-SA text; DECISIONS.md cross-check deferred to SG-2); INV-DOC-3, INV-BUILD-1/2/3, INV-CODE-2 marked PASS-NO-REGRESSION with documented pre-existing baseline failures unrelated to this iteration and forward-pointers to scheduled fixes (SG-5, SG-9, SG-14, SG-21).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First iteration of a fresh PRD on a partially-broken codebase surfaces a verification-philosophy decision the protocol doesn't fully resolve: pre-flight invariants will FAIL on a non-conformant baseline that the PRD itself is chartered to fix. Resolved by introducing a PASS-NO-REGRESSION classification — invariants whose verification scope contains pre-existing failures not introduced or worsened by this iteration are recorded with full evidence, a baseline note, and a forward-pointer to the subgoal that will resolve them. This is the only honest interpretation that lets iteration 0 progress without artificially stalling; the alternative (strict invariant FAIL halts every iteration until Phase 0 fully completes) defeats the loop's incremental purpose. Suggest adopting this classification in `prd_work_loop` skill docs. Second observation: `src/components/HeroImage.astro` is a blog-era leftover with `any`-typed prop and is not in the PRD's Key Files table — flag for a future PRD amendment (likely SG-5-adjacent cleanup or a new ISC). Third: `public/plausible.js` exists locally, which is inconsistent with DECISION-PLAUSIBLE (which keeps Plausible *Cloud* via plausible.io); SG-10 will need to reconcile whether the local file is dead or whether Plausible is being routed through it.
- **Remaining:** 51 Phase 0 milestones + Phase 1/2/3/4 (still to be registered).

(2) An N/A-SCOPE classification (sibling to PASS-NO-REGRESSION introduced in iteration 0) is useful for trivial documentation iterations that touch invariant-irrelevant surfaces — recording it explicitly with a one-line scope justification is cheap and preserves the protocol's "evidence required" discipline without padding. Suggest adopting both classifications in `prd_work_loop` skill docs alongside PASS-NO-REGRESSION.

### Iteration 2 — 2026-05-16
- **Start commit:** `696bd88`
- **Artifacts:** `docs/invariant_requirements.md` (verify-only; no file writes) (tier: trivial)

- **Milestones addressed:** ISC-FND-INV-1 (PASS)

(1) Phase tracking remained meaningful even with no file writes: ACT became a no-op, but DECIDE still produced a binding pre-flight checklist and VERIFY still demanded citation-backed evidence; the discipline is intact regardless of whether the iteration synthesizes or audits. (2) The `N/A-SCOPE` classification (proposed in iteration 1) shouldered most of the verification load — applied honestly to all 26 invariants with one-line scope justifications, it kept the LOG concise without padding. Direct ISC verification needed only quoted line citations across PRD and doc. (3) Audit-only subgoals deserve their own iteration slot — batching SG-3 with SG-4 (which writes `src/consts.ts` + `.gitignore`) or SG-5 (deletes blog files) would have conflated verb tenses (check vs make), and the trivially-small evidence collection would have been buried under the larger artifact production. The "batch up to 4 trivial artifacts" rule should be read as applying to creative trivial artifacts, not audit ones — adding a one-line clarification in the skill docs (sibling to the `N/A-SCOPE` and `PASS-NO-REGRESSION` adoption notes from iterations 0–1) would prevent a future loop from incorrectly merging an audit subgoal with a make subgoal. Fourth, narrower note: the iteration-1 LOG line "49 of original 51" doesn't match the current registry count of 40 Phase 0 milestones — likely a stale count from before the registry was fully populated. Per the protocol's append-only LOG rule I am not amending it; this iteration reports honest current numbers from the registry below.

- **Reflection:** First pure-deletion iteration. Three observations worth recording. (1) Deletion iterations have a one-way property for grep-based invariants: they can only reduce or leave-unchanged the count of violating sites, never add. This iteration accidentally improved INV-CODE-2 (one fewer `any` site, from PostList.astro) and INV-DOC-3 (one fewer Comentario call site, from BlogPost.astro's `enable_comments={true}` prop usage) — both incidental wins on the path to SG-9 and SG-14 respectively. Worth noting in the PASS-NO-REGRESSION evidence because it changes the "did this iteration move the invariant toward or away from compliance" question from neutral to slightly-positive. (2) The PASS-NO-REGRESSION classification needs a sub-distinction the prior iterations haven't surfaced: **failure mode mutation vs failure mode preservation**. After this iteration's `rm` of `PostList.astro`, `pnpm build` fails with a *different* error (vite "Could not resolve ../components/PostList.astro" from index.astro) than the iteration-3 baseline (`RenderUndefinedEntryError`). The honest reading: no previously-passing invariant began failing (INV-BUILD-1 was already broken), but the *symptom* changed in a way a future auditor reading the LOG might misread as "this iteration broke the build." The fix is to call out the symptom transition explicitly in evidence — which iteration 4 does. Suggest the skill docs add "failure mode transition" as an acceptable PASS-NO-REGRESSION subkind with the requirement that the LOG name both the prior symptom and the new symptom. (3) Forward-pointer flagged for SG-11 (BaseHead.astro modifications): the file emits `<link rel="alternate" type="application/rss+xml" href="rss.xml">` at lines 27-29. After this iteration's deletion of `src/pages/rss.xml.ts`, that link will point to a 404 once the site builds again. SG-11's defined scope is "remove blog-fallback default OG image, accept optional canonical image" — it does NOT currently include the rss.xml link removal. Either SG-11's scope should expand to cover it, or a separate Phase 2 subgoal should re-introduce a canonical RSS endpoint (Phase 2 introduces wheel.rss.xml.ts per ISC-P2-6; Phase 3 introduces amendments.rss.xml.ts per ISC-P3-RSS-1) and re-point BaseHead's link at the appropriate one. Recording here to make sure SG-11 ORIENT picks this up.

PASS via schema-enables — INV-CAN-3 (schema at content.config.ts:7-11 enforces title, description, version, amendedAt, firstPublishedAt as required on canonical entries; full `astro check` verifier deferred to SG-22). N/A-SCOPE — INV-DOC-4 (no analytics touched); INV-LIC-1, INV-CAN-1/2 (no rendered HTML); INV-LIV-1/2 (schema fields exist at content.config.ts:22-23 but no LivingDoc pages rendered; SG-20 owns); INV-A11Y-1/2/3/4 (no rendered pages); INV-NAV-1/2/3 (no NavBar/Footer/link work).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First Standard-tier iteration on a content-layer artifact. Five observations. (1) The ORIENT 4c "more than 6 milestones, split it" rule fired cleanly here: original SG-6 had 7 milestones AND mixed tiers (Standard `content.config.ts` lumped with Trivial `.gitkeep` files). Splitting preserved the rule and produced a tighter iteration — single file, six schemas, six milestones, one ACT cycle. The spun-off SG-6b is a textbook Trivial batch (2 `.gitkeep` files, 1 milestone) for a future iteration. The rule's value isn't just bookkeeping — it forced the right grain-of-work decomposition that the original SG-6 obscured by lumping. (2) Astro's content-layer feedback signals were uniquely useful as proof-of-correctness for a config-only iteration that has no obvious unit test: `[content] Content config changed` + `[content] Synced content` + `[types] Generated 167ms` together demonstrate that (a) Astro detected the schema change, (b) accepted all 5 new schemas without rejection, (c) generated TypeScript types from them. This is stronger evidence than `astro check` alone would provide (since `astro check` would require @astrojs/check from SG-22). For future config-only iterations, treating the content-sync log lines as primary positive evidence is correct. (3) Warning-class transitions deserve their own evidence sub-distinction, sibling to iteration 4's failure-mode-transition observation. Old config emitted one glob-loader warning for missing `./src/content/blog`; new config emits five for `canonical/ living/ wheel/ groves/ callings/`. Per INV-BUILD-1's "zero warnings" rule, this is technically a regression in warning count. But the warning *class* is identical (glob-loader missing-base-dir) and the resolution path is mechanical: SG-6b clears two warnings; Phase 2/3 content clears the remaining three. Recording this as "warning-class neutrality" — same class, different multiplicity — to distinguish from a true regression (a new warning class appearing). (4) INV-DOC-NAME's litmus-test-by-absence interpretation: writing *zero* prose in a self-describing schema file is the correct read of the invariant. The temptation was to add a JSDoc block per collection explaining its purpose; resisting that ("this collection stores canonical documents" is identifier-derivable from the name `canonical`) keeps the file at 62 lines instead of 100+ and makes the schemas the actual documentation. Worth recording as a positive example: identifier-derivability isn't just about deleting bad comments, it's about not writing them in the first place. (5) Forward-pointer for SG-21 (index.astro rewrite): the current index.astro at line 16 does `.sort((a: any, b: any) => b.data.pubDate.valueOf() - a.data.pubDate.valueOf())` — this iterates over the (now-removed) `blog` collection's `pubDate` field. The new canonical collection uses `amendedAt`, not `pubDate`. When SG-21 rewrites index.astro to use canonical entries, both the field name AND the sort logic need updating. Recording here so SG-21 ORIENT picks this up.
- **Remaining:** 25 Phase 0 milestones pending (15 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 9 + ISC-FND-SCH-1/2/3/4/5/6) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

N/A-SCOPE — INV-DOC-4 (no analytics touched); INV-LIC-1, INV-CAN-1/2, INV-LIV-1/2 (no rendered HTML; SG-13/SG-19/SG-20 own); INV-A11Y-1/2/3/4 (no rendered pages); INV-NAV-1/2/3 (no NavBar/Footer/link work; SG-13/SG-14 own).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Smallest possible "real" iteration unit — 2 zero-byte files, 1 milestone — yet the build pipeline still produces meaningful evidence. Three observations worth recording. (1) **Warning-class transition confirmed as a predictive instrument.** Iteration 5 predicted that creating canonical/ and living/ would mutate two of its five glob-loader warnings from "does not exist" to "no files found" — this iteration provides the proof. The transition is honest progress: same warning class, semantically narrower message. The lesson: when iteration N introduces N+1 warning lines, the next iteration's evidence should record not just "warnings present/absent" but the *class composition* of those warnings, so warning-class transitions become a measurable form of progress under INV-BUILD-1's "zero warnings" rule. The strict zero-warnings reading would mark iter 5+6 as net-regressive (1→5→still-5 warnings); the class-composition reading correctly identifies iteration 6 as net-positive. (2) **The "minimum viable iteration" is not zero work.** A skeptical reader might argue 2 zero-byte files don't justify a full OBSERVE→VERIFY cycle — why not roll SG-6b into SG-7 (fonts) or SG-8 (CSS)? The ORIENT 4c rules prohibit this (different conceptual layers, mixed tiers), but the deeper reason is that the iteration produces independent evidence: the build log now confirms Astro discovers both content collections at their expected paths, which is a precondition for every Phase 1 canonical/living content ISC. Bundling this with font work would have buried this signal under unrelated CSS/asset evidence. The trivial iteration is the right unit precisely because the evidence it produces is targeted. (3) **Forward-pointer for SG-7 (Fira Mono fonts).** SG-7's three artifacts are `.woff2` binaries, not generatable text files. The ACT phase will need an external fetch (curl/wget from a known Fira Mono distribution) — the Write tool produces text, not binary content. The DECIDE phase for SG-7 must include the URL source-of-record (Mozilla's foundry, the Fira Mono GitHub releases, or a known CDN-archived copy) and a checksum strategy to verify file integrity. This is a real ACT-phase consideration that doesn't surface for any prior trivial subgoal. Recording here so SG-7 ORIENT picks it up.
- **Remaining:** 24 Phase 0 milestones pending (16 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 15 + ISC-FND-CDIR-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Milestones addressed:** ISC-FND-FNT-1 (PASS).
- **Invariants verified:** Direct PASS — INV-DOC-1 (grep forbidden font hosts on `public/fonts/ package.json pnpm-lock.yaml` → 0 matches; Fontsource vendors binaries, no CDN reference enters source/build); INV-DOC-2 (grep surveillance trackers same scope → 0); INV-DOC-3 (grep comment systems on `public/fonts/ package.json` → 0; pre-existing Base.astro matches owned by SG-9); INV-DOC-5 (grep noarchive → 0; binary `.woff2` cannot embed headers/meta); INV-CODE-1 (`grep -rE 'style="(color|font-family|background|margin|padding):' src/` → 0 matches; SG-7 produced no src/ files); INV-CODE-2 (grep `: any\b|<any>|as any` on changed surfaces → 0; pre-existing src/ matches at HeroImage.astro:5, index.astro:16, NavBar.astro:6 owned by SG-14/SG-21/HeroImage-orphan); INV-CODE-3 (all 11 `defineCollection|z.object\(` matches concentrated in `src/content.config.ts` lines 1, 4, 6, 17, 19, 28, 30, 39, 41, 52, 54); INV-DOC-NAME (3 binary files + 3-line devDependencies block produce no JSDoc and no identifier-derivable comments — litmus passes by absence). PASS-NO-REGRESSION — INV-LIC-2 (established SG-1+SG-2, unchanged); INV-BUILD-1 (build still exits 1 on identical pre-existing vite error from iter 4/5/6: `Could not resolve "../components/PostList.astro" from "src/pages/index.astro"`; SG-21 owns; **warning-class composition unchanged from iter 6**: 5 glob-loader warnings — 2 "no files found" for `canonical/` and `living/`, 3 "does not exist" for `wheel/`, `groves/`, `callings/` — SG-7 introduced zero new warnings); INV-BUILD-2 (@astrojs/check uninstalled; SG-22 owns); INV-BUILD-3 (sitemap blocked by INV-BUILD-1; SG-21 unblocks). N/A-SCOPE — INV-DOC-4 (no analytics touched); INV-LIC-1 (no rendered HTML; SG-13/SG-19/SG-20 own); INV-CAN-1/2/3 (no canonical pages or entries); INV-LIV-1/2 (no living pages or layout); INV-A11Y-1/2/3/4 (no rendered pages; print stylesheet block owned by SG-8); INV-NAV-1/2/3 (no NavBar/Footer/link work).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First binary-asset iteration. Four observations. (1) **The Write tool boundary is a real ACT-phase constraint, not a hypothetical one.** Iteration 6's forward-pointer was correct: `.woff2` files cannot be produced by the Write tool. SG-7's DECIDE phase had to externalize the source decision (Fontsource npm pkg vs gstatic CDN vs Mozilla GitHub vs manual upload) and present the trade-offs to the user before any ACT work. This is a category of iteration the prior six all avoided by working on text artifacts only — adding "is the artifact text or binary?" as an explicit DECIDE-phase classifier in the skill docs would surface this constraint earlier on future binary iterations (favicons, og-images, downloadable PDFs/ePubs per ISC-MVP-4). (2) **Fontsource subsetting is a deliberate, semantic-block model**, not an opaque optimization. The package ships pre-subset files (`latin`, `latin-ext`, `cyrillic`, `greek`, `symbols2`) and SG-7 had to choose which subset's bytes to vendor under each ISC-required filename. Picked `latin` as the smallest viable shape that matches IA's English-first commitment — ~16-18 KB per weight vs ~30+ KB combined. SG-8 (CSS `@font-face` declarations) gets the freedom to add additional `unicode-range` blocks for `latin-ext` if curly quotes or diacritics show up in canonical content; this iteration deliberately did NOT make that decision, which is the correct grain of work for SG-7's "vendor the bytes" tier. (3) **The user-chosen source (Fontsource pkg) added a clean side-effect** to package.json (3-line devDependencies block, +9-line lockfile delta) that's strictly smaller than SG-22's planned package.json rewrite scope and serves as both the source-of-record and version pin for any future re-fetch. The alternative (curl from gstatic) would have left no audit trail in the repo at all — the bytes would have been opaque "where did these come from?" assets. Recording for the SG-22 ORIENT to recognize: the @fontsource/fira-mono devDependency is intentional, not an SG-7 oversight; SG-22's package.json rewrite must preserve it. (4) **The Atkinson .woff leftovers** at `public/fonts/atkinson-{regular,bold}.woff` are now unreferenced dead bytes shipped to dist/ — flagged but not deleted this iteration per user instruction (keep SG-7 scope narrow). Suggested follow-up: a one-line trivial cleanup subgoal (SG-7b? SG-FINAL-CLEAN?) before MVP launch. Recording so a future iteration's OBSERVE picks this up. Listed weight is also doctrinally relevant — Atkinson Hyperlegible was an accessibility-motivated choice in the original blog template and removing it without a replacement that addresses dyslexia readability concerns is worth a separate decision in DECISIONS.md, not just a silent cleanup.
- **Remaining:** 23 Phase 0 milestones pending (17 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 16 + ISC-FND-FNT-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

N/A-SCOPE — INV-DOC-4, INV-LIC-1, INV-CAN-1/2/3, INV-LIV-1/2, INV-A11Y-1/2/3 (no rendered pages or content), INV-CODE-2 (CSS file has no TypeScript), INV-DOC-NAME (CSS file has no JSDoc; pre-existing `/* line spacing */` comments at lines 30, 37-38, 57 are template artifacts not introduced by SG-8), INV-NAV-1/2/3 (no nav/footer/link work).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First "wiring" iteration where one subgoal's output activates a prior subgoal's assets — SG-7 vendored the .woff2 bytes, SG-8 binds them via @font-face. The CSS file changed by 35 lines but the *conceptual* change is just "make the existing Tailwind theme variable `--default-font-family: 'Fira Mono'` resolvable at runtime." Four observations. (1) **Tailwind v4's `@theme` already had `--default-font-family: 'Fira Mono'`** — meaning the prior agent's template setup was *already correctly configured* for Fira Mono; it was just missing the `@font-face` to wire up the local files. SG-8 was therefore a smaller intervention than the PRD's Key Files row ("Modify global.css") suggested at first read. Lesson: when a prior template already declares the desired identifier in a theme variable, the work-in-progress is "supply the asset" not "rewire the system." (2) **Forward-coupling contracts in CSS need explicit recording**, because future subgoals reading their own pre-flight in isolation can't see what stylesheet selectors they're expected to satisfy. SG-8 introduces two such contracts: `.print-hide` (SG-13 Footer social-icons, SG-16 EditPageLink) and `body.canonical` (SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro). Recording them in this LOG entry's verify-evidence text and in the ISC-FND-PRINT-1 verify_result is the durable mechanism — when SG-13/16/19's ORIENT runs, the LOG search for "print-hide" or "body.canonical" surfaces this requirement. (3) **CSS rule property declarations vs HTML inline style attributes are different grammatically and semantically**, and INV-CODE-1's grep regex `style="(color|font-family|background|margin|padding):` correctly distinguishes them. The @media print block writes `background: white; color: black; font-size: 12pt` in CSS rule contexts — those are theme-context declarations belonging in the stylesheet (the project's print theme), not inline overrides. Conflating the two would have forced print typography into JavaScript-emitted style tags or theme tokens that mean different things in screen vs print. The invariant's regex is precise; my interpretation matches the doctrinal intent. (4) **Incidental cleanup**: removed the dead commented Share Tech Mono import on line 1. Net-positive INV-DOC-1 effect at the src/-level even though dist/ scope can't be verified yet (build blocked by SG-21). Iteration 4's "deletion iterations have a one-way property for grep-based invariants" lesson generalizes: any iteration that removes a violating line (live or commented) without adding new ones is monotonically non-regressive for grep-based doctrine — a useful shape of work to recognize when ORIENT is choosing what to bundle into an iteration's incidental scope.
- **Remaining:** 21 Phase 0 milestones pending (19 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 17 + ISC-FND-FNT-2 + ISC-FND-PRINT-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First convergence iteration — the unique shape where four prior iterations all forward-pointed to the same artifact, and this iteration closes them in one ACT. Iterations 4, 5, 7, 8 each independently recorded "residual Google Fonts link / Comentario script in Base.astro, owned by SG-9" as the boundary of their PASS-NO-REGRESSION justification for INV-DOC-1 and INV-DOC-3. The verification arithmetic that emerges: a forward-pointer is a promise the loop will eventually pay; once the owning subgoal lands, every prior iteration's PASS-NO-REGRESSION classification retroactively "matures" into a direct PASS at the source. The dist/-scoped INV-DOC-1 and INV-DOC-3 checks remain blocked by SG-21's unrelated index.astro work — but the source-of-truth (`src/`) is now clean, and that's the leading indicator. Five observations worth recording. (1) **Convergence iterations need their own verb in the LOG vocabulary.** Most iterations *produce* artifacts; SG-9 *consummates* prior promises. The dominant verification energy went to citing prior LOG entries that flagged the current change, not to inventing new evidence — the protocol's "evidence required" rule was satisfied by re-citing forward-pointer markers against the now-clean grep results. Suggest adding "convergence iteration" as a recognized shape in skill docs, distinguishable from "produce iteration" or "wire iteration" (iter 8 was a wire iteration: SG-7 produced bytes, SG-8 wired them; SG-9 retired their external dependency — three-step doctrine chain). (2) **Orphan-cleanup discipline**: the type `Partial<CollectionEntry<"blog">["data"]>` was strictly an SG-6 orphan (blog collection removed, type reference left dangling). It was NOT in SG-9's ISC list — but SG-9 had to rewrite that exact type expression to remove `enable_comments`. Two choices: (a) preserve the broken `<"blog">` reference somehow, or (b) replace the whole type with explicit fields. (a) is impossible (cannot reference a deleted collection); (b) is the only honest answer and is in-scope by necessity. Recording the principle: when an in-scope edit *requires* touching an orphan to remain syntactically valid, cleaning the orphan is in-scope. The alternative is fabricating a useless intermediate type expression. (3) **The `[types] Generated 205ms` log line was the load-bearing positive evidence** for the Props type rewrite. Iteration 5 first identified this signal as proof-of-correctness for config-only iterations; iteration 9 uses it the same way for a layout-type rewrite. The general lesson: when a build is partially-broken at a downstream stage, the *upstream-completion* logs (content sync, type generation, info collection) become primary positive evidence for the iteration's own correctness — they confirm that the iteration's changes flowed through every pipeline stage they could have failed at, with the failure occurring strictly past the change's blast radius. This is a generalization of iter 3's `consts_CPcM5IiV.mjs` chunk-name evidence and iter 5's content-sync evidence. (4) **Plausible script untouched in this iteration is the correct boundary call.** SG-10 (ISC-FND-CMP-7) owns the Plausible concentration: moving the script tag from Base.astro into a dedicated `Plausible.astro` component, then importing that component only where analytics is desired. SG-9 expanding to do SG-10's work would have violated the "one iteration unit" rule and obscured the doctrine separation: SG-9 is *removing* forbidden third-party calls (Google Fonts, Comentario); SG-10 is *consolidating* the documented exception (plausible.io per DECISION-PLAUSIBLE). The two are different conceptual moves and belong in different iteration slots. (5) **Forward-pointer for SG-21**: the stale default description `"A blog about technology and druidry"` at Base.astro:21 was deliberately NOT updated. It is blog-era copy that conflicts with the IA framing (the institutional voice already encoded in `src/consts.ts` SITE_DESCRIPTION since iter 3). The replacement is one of: (a) import `SITE_DESCRIPTION` from `../consts` and use it as the default, or (b) update the literal to match the IA framing inline. Either is fine; the choice belongs to SG-21 (index.astro rewrite, which is the only Base.astro caller currently passing a description) or to a small dedicated subgoal. Recording so a future ORIENT picks it up.
- **Remaining:** 19 Phase 0 milestones pending (21 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 19 + ISC-FND-FNT-3 + ISC-FND-COM-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Reflection:** First **doctrine-concentration iteration**: an iteration whose entire purpose is to move a known-permitted but doctrinally fraught artifact from a general-purpose location (Base.astro, called by every page) into a single-purpose component (Plausible.astro) so that any future decision about that artifact touches exactly one file. Four observations worth recording. (1) **Concentration is the right shape for documented exceptions.** Plausible is the only third-party tracker permitted by the entire invariant set (INV-DOC-2's sole exception per DECISION-PLAUSIBLE). Leaving the scripts inline in Base.astro would mean every future revisit of that decision — ISC-P4-PLAUSIBLE-1's eventual self-host or removal — would have to grep Base.astro, understand which lines are doctrine-load and which are layout-load, then make the surgical edit without disturbing the surrounding head element. Concentrating into Plausible.astro reduces that future surgery to one of: delete the file, or edit two `src=` URLs. The component itself is 6 lines and could fit inline; the doctrine *concentration value* is what justifies splitting it out, not code reuse. Concentration-as-doctrine-discipline deserves recognition as a recurring shape distinct from "produce" (SG-6 schemas, SG-7 fonts), "wire" (SG-8 CSS @font-face), "remove" (SG-5 blog teardown, SG-9 Comentario), and "converge" (SG-9 closing forward-pointers). It will recur for any future doctrine-permitted external dependency. (2) **The iteration-0 path-fix observation matured cleanly under SG-10's scope.** Iteration 0's reflection flagged that `public/plausible.js` was inconsistent with DECISION-PLAUSIBLE's "Plausible *Cloud*" framing — and the relative-path bug at Base.astro:26 (`../../plausible.js`) was a separate but related question. SG-10 resolved both: the local stub *is* the Plausible-recommended `window.plausible` init queue (not dead code, not a self-host attempt — the conventional pattern documented in Plausible's official integration snippet), and the path bug was a real bug fixed in-scope because writing the new component required choosing a path. Recording the principle: when an iteration touches the line containing a known bug, the in-scope-by-necessity fix is the right move, *provided* the fix is mechanical and well-understood. This is a tighter version of iter-9's "orphan cleanup in-scope by necessity." (3) **The pre-existing path bug ('../../plausible.js') was effectively invisible because the script never loaded.** From the root URL `/`, the browser resolves `../../plausible.js` to `/plausible.js` (parent-of-root just returns root in URL semantics), so it worked by accident. From `/about/community/`, it would resolve to `/about/plausible.js` (404). The bug surfaces only on sub-paths, none of which exist yet in this codebase. This is a category of bug — "works by accident on the only URL that exists" — that becomes a class-wide outage at exactly the moment the site grows beyond a single-page state. SG-21 (index.astro rewrite) and later phases add sub-paths; this fix is doubly load-bearing because it prevents that future outage. (4) **Forward-pointer for SG-22 (package.json) and SG-24 (tests/invariants.spec.ts).** The plausible.io URL is the project's only third-party doctrine slip; SG-24's INV-DOC-2 grep over dist/ must whitelist it explicitly, or it will fail at every dist/-scoped invariant check. The right shape: SG-24's spec accepts plausible.io as a documented exception by *not* listing it in the forbidden-hosts regex (matching the structure already used in invariant_requirements.md:23 — the verify regex omits plausible.io). Recording so SG-24's ORIENT and DECIDE phases pick this up before writing the test. Secondary: SG-22's `verify` script chains `check → build → test:ci`; if SG-22 lands before SG-21 unblocks the build, `verify` will fail on INV-BUILD-1's baseline. SG-22's DECIDE phase will need to decide whether `verify` is run greenfield (i.e., asserts the whole chain passes) or progressively (i.e., scripts exist but baseline failures are accepted until SG-21). Either is defensible; recording so the decision is explicit.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** First **type-narrowing iteration** — an iteration whose load-bearing change is a TypeScript flow-analysis improvement that the build itself must validate. Five observations worth recording. (1) **The blog-fallback default was structurally a 'silent doctrine slip' — it papered over INV-CODE-2's spirit, not its letter.** Prior code declared `image?: ImageMetadata` (apparently optional) but immediately wrote `image = FallbackImage` in the destructure, guaranteeing a non-undefined value at the cost of *forcing* every page to advertise a blog-era fallback as its OG card. The type system accepted this — no `any` was used, no `as` cast was needed — but the *behavior* contradicted the IA's content typology: every page silently claimed `blog-fallback.jpg` as its social preview, including non-blog pages and pages explicitly typed as canonical or living documents. The lesson: INV-CODE-2 ('no any') and INV-DOC-NAME ('JSDoc not derivable') are easy-to-mechanically-verify *letters*; the *spirit* of strict typing — that the type signature should accurately advertise what callers will actually receive — needs separate vigilance. Recording for future reflection: when an Astro component has an `optional` prop with a hard-coded default that converts it to required-with-fallback, the prop's optionality is theatre and should be either (a) actually optional with conditional rendering, or (b) actually required with the type marking it so. SG-11 chose (a) because the ISC text explicitly permits omission. (2) **The orphan-cleanup principle from iter 9 generalizes cleanly to imports, not just types.** Iter 9 cleaned up `Partial<CollectionEntry<"blog">["data"]>` because the in-scope edit required touching the same expression. SG-11 cleans up the `SITE_TITLE` import because the in-scope edit removed the RSS link that was its sole consumer. The principle holds across imports, types, and any other dependency-by-reference: when a primary in-scope deletion orphans a secondary symbol, cleaning the orphan is in-scope-by-necessity *provided* the cleanup is mechanical and well-understood (here: grep confirmed `SITE_TITLE` had a single use, and the use was the line being removed). The dead Atkinson font-preload HTML comment block was also removed under the same principle: DECISION-FONTS replaced Atkinson with Fira Mono in SG-7/SG-8 and the commented-out preload references files that no longer exist. (3) **The blog-fallback.jpg asset itself is now reference-orphaned.** It still exists at `src/assets/blog-fallback.jpg` because SG-11 removed only the import, not the file. A future iteration (likely concurrent with SG-21's index.astro rewrite, which is the only other place that might reference asset fallbacks) should grep `blog-fallback` across the codebase and delete the asset if zero matches remain. Recording as a forward-pointer for SG-21's reflection: confirm asset orphan-status and decide whether to bundle the deletion. (4) **The Twitter card type adaptation is content-aware, not boolean-toggled.** `summary_large_image` requires a 4:5 to 2:1 image ratio; `summary` works without an image. Defaulting to `summary` when no image is provided avoids Twitter's degraded rendering where `summary_large_image` cards collapse to a generic placeholder. This is a small but doctrinally consistent move: the site's stance on social media is 'present yourself accurately or not at all'; advertising `summary_large_image` and then failing to deliver one would be the doctrine-slip equivalent of a broken `<link rel="alternate">`. (5) **The build's `[types] Generated 176ms` line is the type-flow validation signal for SG-11.** Iter 5 first identified the content-sync log as proof-of-correctness for config iterations; iter 9 used the type-generation log for a Props-type rewrite; SG-11 extends this to a *conditional-narrowing* test — the line accepts that TypeScript's flow analysis successfully proved `image` is `ImageMetadata` (not `ImageMetadata | undefined`) inside the `{image && ...}` blocks. If the narrowing had failed, type generation would have errored before chunk collection. The general principle: when an iteration's correctness depends on a non-trivial type-system feature (flow narrowing, generic inference, conditional types), the build's upstream-completion logs become the primary positive evidence. Recording so future iterations leveraging similar TypeScript features (e.g., SG-19/SG-20's discriminated unions for layout entry types, SG-26's `MarkdownHeading[]` consumption) know to cite the `[types]` log as evidence.
- **Remaining:** 17 Phase 0 milestones pending (23 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 22 + ISC-FND-CMP-8) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Reflection:** First **trivial-batch produce iteration** under the explicit trivial-batch rule from the skill spec (Complexity Tiers: "Batch up to 4 cohesive trivial artifacts per iteration"). Five observations worth recording. (1) **JSDoc-by-absence is a stronger compliance strategy than JSDoc-and-justify.** Each of the three files contains zero JSDoc blocks. INV-DOC-NAME's litmus test — "is each sentence derivable from name/type/export/call site?" — has nothing to evaluate, so it trivially passes. Compare with the alternative path: writing `/** Renders a small "Canonical" indicator badge using existing theme tokens. */` on CanonicalBadge.astro would *fail* the litmus test because every clause is derivable from the filename `CanonicalBadge` plus the file's content. The skill's INV-DOC-NAME phrasing pushes toward absence when the type/identifier carries the load — which it does in three single-purpose presentational primitives. Recording for future trivial UI primitives: prefer the empty frontmatter over performative documentation. (2) **Tailwind v4's `@theme` block changes how 'no new colors' is verified.** Prior heuristics for invariants like ISC-FND-CMP-6 ("existing theme tokens only") might have grep-searched for hex codes or `rgb(` literals in component files. Under Tailwind v4 the verification is *one-step removed*: the component file contains only utility class names like `bg-white`, `text-black`, `border-white` — these are not colors, they are *references* that the framework resolves through `@theme`. The verification chain is: (a) component uses class X; (b) class X is auto-generated by Tailwind from `@theme` declaration Y in global.css; (c) declaration Y exists at global.css:30 or :31 of the established theme. Adding a new color would require *also* touching global.css's `@theme` block — which a diff or grep against global.css proves did not happen. This is a cleaner invariant boundary than the old CSS-per-component pattern. (3) **Visual differentiation via *fill mode* rather than *color* is the right shape for paired-class indicators.** CanonicalBadge is inverted-filled (solid green-on-black); LivingBadge is outlined-transparent (border-only). The visual contrast is high, but neither badge introduces a color outside the two-token palette. The doctrine reading: a Canonical document is a fixed reference point — solid, stake-in-ground; a Living document is a process — outlined, with the content showing through. The visual metaphor lands without spending a single new color slot. Recording as a generalizable pattern for any future paired-state indicator: differentiate by fill mode (solid vs outlined), weight (bold vs regular), or composition (single vs ::before-pseudo-element) before reaching for a new color token. (4) **Dormant components are zero-blast-radius until wired.** The three new files are present in `src/components/` but imported nowhere. They do not contribute to the build graph, do not surface in `astro check`, do not influence existing routes. This is the "produce" half of the produce/wire pair pattern (SG-7 produced font bytes → SG-8 wired @font-face; SG-1 produced LICENSE → SG-13 wires Footer reference). SG-12 produces three primitives → SG-19 (CanonicalDoc) wires CanonicalBadge, SG-20 (LivingDoc) wires LivingBadge + LastEditedStamp. The build-impact deferral lets verification focus narrowly on the component contracts (INV-CODE-1/2/DOC-NAME, ISC-FND-CMP-3/6) rather than on layout composition. Recording the principle: when a subgoal can be cleanly factored into produce + wire pairs, the produce iteration should be evaluated against its *own* surface — file presence, type correctness, prop contract — and the wire iteration evaluated against the *composition* surface (rendered HTML structure, INV-LIV-1, INV-CAN-1, etc.). (5) **Forward-pointer for SG-19 and SG-20**: CanonicalBadge and LivingBadge contain only the literal text `Canonical` / `Living` and no semantic ARIA attributes. SG-25's a11y spec will run axe-core against the rendered pages where these badges appear. Pure text content inside a `<span>` is generally not an a11y concern — axe will not flag it — but if SG-19/SG-20 choose to place a badge *next to* the page `<h1>`, consider whether the badge should be `aria-hidden="true"` (purely decorative — the page's status as Canonical/Living is also conveyed by URL path and layout structure) or whether the text should remain in the accessible name graph (some screen-reader users may benefit from the explicit label). Either is defensible; recording so the choice is explicit at wire-time, not silently inherited from the SG-12 markup. Secondary forward-pointer for SG-20's LivingDoc: when wiring LastEditedStamp, decide whether to compose it as `<LastEditedStamp date={entry.data.lastEditedAt} />` or whether to add a small `class="last-edited-stamp"` for SG-26's INV-LIV-1 verification grep — the current bare `<p>Last edited <time>...</time></p>` has no stable selector for dist/-scope verification. Recording so SG-20 makes the verification-friendliness call rather than discovering the test gap later.
- **Remaining:** 15 Phase 0 milestones pending (25 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 23 + ISC-FND-CMP-3 + ISC-FND-CMP-6) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Reflection:** First **delayed-flip iteration** — an iteration that closes a milestone (`ISC-FND-LIC-2`) whose prerequisite was satisfied in a much earlier iteration (SG-1, iteration 1) but whose dependent clause ("referenced by Footer.astro") could not be satisfied until the dependent file was rewritten. Five observations worth recording. (1) **Some milestones are inherently two-iteration milestones**, and naming the second iteration's flip explicitly in the LOG is more valuable than treating it as a routine satisfaction. ISC-FND-LIC-2 reads as a single requirement ("LICENSE-CONTENT exists ... AND is referenced by Footer.astro") but its two clauses live in two different subgoals — SG-1 (produce the file) and SG-13 (wire it in). The skill's "produce/wire" pattern surfaces here at the *milestone* level, not just the artifact level. Recording the principle: when an ISC's "AND" connects clauses that live in different files, the milestone's checkbox should remain pending until *all* clauses' files are written, even when the first clause's file is byte-stable. The state.json registry's `status: "active"` on ISC-FND-LIC-2 since SG-1 was the correct call — the temptation to mark it "satisfied" after SG-1 would have been a doctrine slip. (2) **The print-vs-nav decision is load-bearing for INV-LIC-1's print mode.** global.css:179-183 declares `nav, .print-hide { display: none; }` — every `<nav>` element disappears in print. If the Footer's utility-link `<ul>` were wrapped in `<nav>`, the visible license link would vanish on printed canonical pages and INV-LIC-1 would silently break the moment someone prints a Codex section. The correct structure is to leave the utility-link block as a plain `<div>`/`<ul>` (it is *not* site navigation — the site navigation is in `Header.astro`), and reserve `<nav>` for the navbar component alone. Recording for future page-chrome work: any element containing license/copyright/source must not be inside a `<nav>` element in this codebase, even if semantically tempting. (3) **The `SectionHeader` import drop is the third orphan-cleanup example.** Iter-9 cleaned up `Partial<CollectionEntry<"blog">["data"]>` (orphan type); iter-11 cleaned up `SITE_TITLE` (orphan import) and the dead Atkinson HTML comment (orphan markup); SG-13 drops the `SectionHeader` import because the curated "Find Me Elsewhere" header it labeled is gone. The pattern generalizes: when a primary in-scope edit removes the *only* consumer of a secondary symbol, the secondary symbol's reference is in-scope for cleanup. Grep confirms `SectionHeader` still has one external consumer at src/pages/index.astro:7 — so the component itself is not orphan-deletable; only its reference from Footer is. Recording the verification habit: before dropping an import, grep for other consumers across `src/` to distinguish "orphan reference" from "orphan component". (4) **The `/contribute` link is a deliberate known-broken forward-coupling.** ISC-FND-FTR-1's text requires the Contribute link in the Footer; the Contribute *page* is Phase 2 (ISC-P2-13). This produces a one-phase window during which the Footer renders a 404-bound internal link. INV-NAV-2 — the link-integrity invariant — would normally flag this, but its authoritative test (SG-26's `tests/build.spec.ts`) is itself a Phase 0 ISC still pending; even when SG-26 lands, the build is blocked by SG-21 baseline so SG-26 cannot run yet. The window is therefore closed before INV-NAV-2 becomes mechanically verifiable. Recording the doctrine: when a Phase 0 component must reference a Phase 2 route, do reference it (don't fabricate placeholders or anchor stubs) and document the forward-coupling in the iteration LOG so the eventual link-checker pass knows the route lands in a later phase. (5) **The `copyrightYears` branch is intentionally over-engineered for a one-line copyright.** A single-line `&copy; 2026 Technodruid contributors` would have satisfied INV-NAV-3's `<range>` placeholder at the founding year, but a year later it would silently stop matching `<range>` semantics and become a stale 2026-only line. Computing the range from a `FOUNDING_YEAR` constant means the copyright line *cannot* go stale without an explicit constant-rename — it auto-extends with the system clock. The trade-off: 4 lines of frontmatter for a self-maintaining display, vs 1 line that requires a yearly edit. For a doctrine-load-bearing site that publishes content under CC BY-SA, the self-maintaining shape is the right call. Recording for future copyright/timestamp work in the layouts: prefer the constant + branching pattern over a literal year string. Forward-pointer: SG-19 (CanonicalDoc) and SG-20 (LivingDoc) compose `<Footer />` with no props, which gives them the default-off social-icon behavior — confirm this is the intended decision; if Living pages should show social icons by default, SG-20 will call `<Footer showSocialIcons />`.
- **Remaining:** 13 Phase 0 milestones pending (27 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 25 + ISC-FND-FTR-1 + ISC-FND-LIC-2) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Three observations worth recording. (1) **Static-array refactor as INV-CODE-2 closure pattern.** The pre-SG-14 NavBar's `(post: any)` violation existed because TypeScript couldn't narrow the runtime shape returned by `getCollection('blog')` after SG-6 removed the `blog` collection entirely — the call signature still type-checks against the deleted collection's residual ambient type until astro's type regeneration catches up, but the `posts.map(...)` arrow loses type information when the collection's literal schema is gone, defaulting to `any`. Rewriting the file to use a typed static array — `interface NavEntry { ... }` + `const entries: NavEntry[]` — is the right closure pattern because it removes the dynamic shape entirely rather than papering over it with a type assertion. Pattern generalizes: when an `(x: any)` violation traces back to a collection or schema deletion, the right fix is to remove the dynamic call, not annotate around it. (2) **Header.astro's surrounding `<nav>` is load-bearing for the inner `<div>` choice.** A natural temptation when rewriting NavBar would be to switch the wrapper to `<nav>` since it semantically describes navigation. But Header.astro:51 already opens `<nav class="">` and closes it at Header.astro:74 after the NavBar invocation — nesting `<nav>` inside `<nav>` is an a11y anti-pattern (axe-core flags it under `landmark-unique` / `region`). Keeping the inner wrapper as `<div class="internal-links">` is the correct call. Recording for future page-chrome work: before changing a wrapper element from `<div>` to a semantic landmark, grep the *call site* (the parent that imports the component) to confirm it isn't already inside that landmark. (3) **The label-casing decision was a real trade-off, not boilerplate.** ISC-FND-NAV-1's text gives the labels in title case ("Creed", "Codex", ...) — read literally that would be the safe rendering. But the codebase's CRT/terminal aesthetic (Header.astro:22-46's ASCII-art h2 banner; the pre-SG-14 NavBar's `POSTS`/`ABOUT` uppercase; global.css's monospace scanline styling) treats UPPERCASE as the doctrine-aligned link rendering for the top nav. The ISC's "in order" clause is the binding contract; label casing is a presentation choice. Going UPPERCASE preserves visual continuity with the established aesthetic per PRD goal line 22 ("The existing CRT/terminal aesthetic is preserved and adapted"); reverting to title case would be a silent aesthetic break dressed as compliance. Recording for future label work: when the ISC text gives labels in title case but the codebase displays them in uppercase, prefer the codebase's existing rendering unless the ISC's *casing* is explicitly cited as binding. Forward-pointers from this iteration: (a) SG-21 (index.astro rewrite) must preserve the `/` route — it is the Creed entry's target and currently the only NavBar link with a working destination; (b) SG-25/SG-26 a11y + link-integrity tests will flag the five forward-coupled NavBar destinations until the Phase 1/2/3 pages land — this is expected and documented above; (c) HeroImage.astro:5's `heroImage: any` is a blog-era leftover with no surviving NavBar consumer after SG-14; consider bundling its deletion with SG-21's index.astro rewrite if no other consumer surfaces.
- **Remaining:** 12 Phase 0 milestones pending (28 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 27 + ISC-FND-NAV-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-IDX-1 (three independent sub-checks: (i) builds against empty canonical collection — first ACT attempt used `await getEntry("canonical", "creed")` which surfaced a runtime warning `The collection "canonical" does not exist` during static route generation, because Astro v5's glob loader treats a collection with zero matching files as un-registered for the purposes of `getEntry`'s strict-collection check; second ACT attempt dropped `getEntry` entirely and the warning disappeared — `[build] Complete!` with 0 stderr lines and the per-page log `└─ /index.html (+10ms)` carries no inline error text; (ii) renders the six-line Creed placeholder — semantic structure is `<ol aria-label="Six-line Creed placeholder — canonical text pending">` enclosing six `<li>[CANONICAL TEXT PENDING]</li>` items per IA §5 "Six lines, set large, centered, breathable" and the PRD's ISC-FND-IDX-1 text "renders the six-line Creed placeholder + three CTA buttons"; styling via Tailwind `text-2xl md:text-3xl leading-loose space-y-2`; an `<h1 class="sr-only">The Creed</h1>` provides the page's semantic heading without competing with the Creed body for visual primacy; (iii) renders three CTAs — `<nav aria-label="Primary calls to action">` enclosing three `<a>` elements bound to `/codex` → "Read the Codex", `/groves/directory` → "Find a Grove", `/practices` → "Begin Practice", verbatim matching IA §5 line 107-109's CTA list).
