SG-26's `tests/build.spec.ts` owns mechanical link-integrity verification once destination pages exist; same pattern as SG-13's `/contribute` and SG-14's NavBar forward-coupling — do not fabricate placeholder pages, reference the canonical IA §4 / §5 routes and document the forward-coupling here).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Four observations worth recording. (1) **INT-PROC-1 unification surfaces a latent baseline failure.** Iterations 4-14 each carried the pre-existing vite `Could not resolve "../components/PostList.astro" from "src/pages/index.astro"` failure as a known baseline owned by SG-21, marking subgoals PASS while the build exited 1. This was a defensible iteration-level call (the failure was not caused by the iteration's artifact) but became indefensible the moment INT-PROC-1 was added to the invariants doc, because INT-PROC-1's text — "an iteration is not complete if there is a build failure or a typecheck failure" — makes no exception for inherited baselines. Lesson for future PRDs: when a new invariant is added mid-PRD that retroactively contradicts the accepted operational pattern, the prd_work_loop must surface this through OBSERVE/ORIENT (which it did) and the iteration owner must escalate to the user rather than rationalize forward (which the AskUserQuestion flow handled). The pattern would also generalize: when a deletion subgoal (here SG-5: delete PostList.astro) leaves a downstream caller orphaned, the orphan-fix subgoal (here SG-21) should be sequenced *before* the deletion completes, or co-bundled with it. Forward-pointer for any future PRD: deletion subgoals should explicitly list their downstream callers and the subgoal that re-points each. (2) **Astro v5's `getEntry` runtime warning is content-coupled, not configuration-coupled.** First ACT attempt's `await getEntry("canonical", "creed")` against the empty canonical collection emitted the runtime message `The collection "canonical" does not exist. Please ensure it is defined in your content config.` — but the collection *is* defined in src/content.config.ts:4-15 per SG-6. The diagnostic message is misleading: Astro v5's glob loader treats a collection with zero matching files as "not registered" for the purposes of `getEntry`'s strict-collection check, even though the collection definition exists. Two takeaways: (a) for Phase 0 transitional pages, do not pre-implement the populated-collection code path — Phase 1's ISC-MVP-2 rewrite will reintroduce `getEntry` against a populated collection naturally; (b) the cleanest Phase 0 form is unconditional placeholder rendering. Premature accommodation of a future state adds dead branches and surfacing-only warnings. (3) **INV-BUILD-1's stderr-vs-stdout distinction is load-bearing.** The invariant doc's operational verification specifies "stderr is empty of warning lines" — a precise test, not "the build has no warnings anywhere in its output." Astro routes `[WARN]` to stdout and `[ERROR]` to stderr; the 5 content-directory `[WARN]` lines do not contravene the invariant. Past iteration LOGs have been ambiguous about whether INV-BUILD-1 was passing or failing on these warnings; iter-15 establishes the strict verification path. Lesson: when an invariant document specifies an operational test (as opposed to a property), honor the *test* — not a related-but-stricter property someone might infer from the invariant's name. (4) **Forward-pointers as a closure mechanism work better when the originating iteration's reflection names them explicitly.** Iter-5's forward-pointer ("line 16 sorts on blog.pubDate — switch to canonical.amendedAt with updated sort logic") and iter-9's forward-pointer ("consider passing SITE_DESCRIPTION from consts") were both closed in this iteration — but only one was closed by *applying* the suggestion (iter-9's was actioned), while the other (iter-5's) was closed by *superseding* the entire code path. The reflection's prediction of how it would close was wrong, but the forward-pointer still functioned: it gave the next implementer a clear signal of where the iter-5 author expected attention. Recording for future reflections: forward-pointers don't need to predict their resolution mechanism, only their location. Forward-pointers from this iteration: (a) HeroImage.astro is now reference-orphaned in src/ — the only callers were the deleted blog rendering paths; deletion candidate when SG-25 / SG-26 confirm no axe/a11y / build-test consumer surfaces a reference; (b) the H2-before-H1 structural pattern (Header.astro:52's brand-logo `<h2>` preceding index.astro's `<h1 class="sr-only">The Creed</h1>` in DOM order) will likely be flagged by SG-25's first axe-core run under `page-has-heading-one` or `heading-order`; the cleanest fix is to demote Header.astro's `<h2>` to a `<div>` (the brand-logo is visually a heading but doesn't need to be a heading semantically) — propose as a future cleanup ISC; (c) the `getEntry` re-introduction path is owned by Phase 1 ISC-MVP-2's rewrite of index.astro; that rewrite will land alongside src/content/canonical/creed.md (ISC-MVP-1) so the empty-collection runtime warning does not resurface.
- **Remaining:** 11 Phase 0 milestones pending (29 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 28 + ISC-FND-IDX-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

PARTIAL-CONTRIBUTION — INV-NAV-2 (Breadcrumbs is not yet rendered in current dist — no layout wraps it; integration is owned by SG-19 — CanonicalDoc.astro — and SG-20 — LivingDoc.astro. When integrated, link targets are drawn from `labelMap` which is grounded in IA §4 canonical routes; mechanical link-integrity verification is owned by SG-26's `tests/build.spec.ts`. Same forward-coupling pattern as NavBar/SG-14 + index.astro CTAs/SG-21).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Three observations worth recording. (1) **`<nav>`-as-print-hide is structurally cleaner than `.print-hide`-as-opt-in.** The Footer.astro/SG-13 pattern applies `.print-hide` explicitly to the social-icons block as a manual opt-in. Breadcrumbs could have done the same, but instead leverages global.css:180's `nav { display: none; }` rule via wrapping the trail in `<nav aria-label="Breadcrumb">` — a single element that satisfies both the W3C ARIA breadcrumb landmark contract *and* the print-suppression behavior. Lesson for SG-15/SG-16/SG-19/SG-20 forward: page-chrome elements that are inherently navigation (breadcrumbs, edit-link toolbars, TOC) should use `<nav>` and inherit print-hiding for free; only non-nav chrome (social icons, comment widgets, search bars) needs explicit `.print-hide`. The SG-16 EditPageLink and SG-18 TableOfContents should both consider wrapping in `<nav>` instead of adding `.print-hide`. (2) **Build-loop construction of `aria-current` is cleaner than post-loop mutation.** A natural pattern would be `crumbs.push({ ..., current: false })` then `crumbs[crumbs.length - 1].current = true` after the loop. Setting `current: index === segments.length - 1` inside the `forEach` carries the invariant directly and avoids the mutation step — the crumb is born with its final state. Generalizes: for any "mark the last item in a built sequence" pattern, prefer in-loop computation over post-loop mutation. (3) **Graceful-fallback as IA-evolution insurance.** The PRD's Key Files table currently fixes 24 IA §4 routes, and `labelMap` enumerates exactly those 24. But Phase 2/3 dynamic routes — `/practices/wheel/[date]`, `/groves/[slug]`, `/callings/[slug]`, future translation prefixes — will produce path segments not in the map. The fallback `labelMap[cumulative] ?? (segment.charAt(0).toUpperCase() + segment.slice(1).replace(/-/g, " "))` means Breadcrumbs degrades to title-cased segment labels rather than crashing or rendering empty crumbs. This is defensive without being defensive-for-its-own-sake — the labelMap remains the authoritative IA §4 source for canonical routes, and the fallback only activates for IA-extension paths. Lesson: when a component renders user-facing labels from a known enum, prefer `enum ?? humanizedFallback` over `enum ?? throw` — the enum carries the canonical source, the fallback carries operational resilience. Forward-pointers from this iteration: (a) the SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro layout should include `<Breadcrumbs />` per its ISC text and inherit the `<nav>`-print-hide pattern established here; (b) the SG-20 LivingDoc.astro layout same; (c) when SG-25 / SG-26 run, the labelMap's exact-route lookups will be silently validated against the rendered NavBar + CanonicalDoc + LivingDoc page paths — any IA §4 mismatch surfaces as a fallback-label render in tests; (d) one structural choice not yet exercised: at very deep paths (4+ segments) the `<ol class="flex flex-wrap items-center gap-x-2">` will wrap onto multiple lines on narrow viewports — this is the desired behavior for accessibility (no horizontal scrolling) and the IA §4 routes max out at 2 segments (`/about/community`) plus likely 3 for Phase 2/3 dynamic routes, so the visual treatment is durable.
- **Remaining:** 10 Phase 0 milestones pending (30 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 29 + ISC-FND-CMP-4) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

The iter-15/16 green-build baseline holds — no regression from adding the new component); INT-PROC-1 (same build evidence as INV-BUILD-1: exit 0, stderr empty; no build failure between iter-16 and iter-17. Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-CMP-2 (three independent sub-checks: (1) prop accepted — line 5 `sourcePath: string;` inside `interface Props` carries the typed declaration; line 8 `const { sourcePath } = Astro.props;` destructures it; the PRD line 241 specifies `sourcePath: string` and this is verbatim what the interface declares; (2) edit-URL construction — line 10 ``const editUrl = `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/edit/main/${normalized}`;`` constructs the URL exactly as PRD line 241 specifies ("builds an edit URL from `SOURCE_REPO_URL` + `/edit/main/` + sourcePath"); the `normalized` interpolation at line 9 is `sourcePath.replace(/^\/+/, "")` which trims any leading slashes — defensive against the natural ambiguity of "should sourcePath include a leading slash?" so the joined URL never produces `/edit/main//foo`; PRD line 241 does not specify the leading-slash convention, so this is a reasonable implementation choice; (3) anchor emission — line 13 `<a class="print-hide" href={editUrl} rel="nofollow">Edit this page</a>` renders the Edit link with the constructed URL; `rel="nofollow"` is a deliberate addition — an Edit link points to a write-action URL space that search engines have no business crawling; consistent with the IA's "respect-the-archive" doctrine which cares about discovery, not write-action visibility). PASS-NO-REGRESSION — INV-LIC-1 (`grep -E 'creativecommons.org/licenses/by-sa/4.0|rel="license"' dist/index.html` → match present via Footer.astro/SG-13 chain; iter-17 introduces no source change to license-emission paths); INV-LIC-2 (`ls LICENSE LICENSE-CONTENT` → both present at repo root from SG-1, untouched); INV-NAV-1 (NavBar's six IA §4 entries unchanged from SG-14); INV-NAV-3 (Footer chain unchanged from SG-13). N/A-SCOPE — INV-DOC-4 (`grep -nE '<script' src/components/EditPageLink.astro` → 0 matches; EditPageLink emits zero `<script>` tags — analytics surface remains concentrated in Plausible.astro per SG-10); INV-CAN-1/2/3 (EditPageLink is layout-agnostic and unrelated to canonical version/amendedAt/source-link markup; concerns owned by VersionFooter + CanonicalDoc + content.config.ts schema — SG-17/SG-19/SG-6); INV-LIV-1 (LastEditedStamp + contributors owned by SG-12 + SG-20; this iteration owns only the Edit-link half of LivingDoc chrome); INV-A11Y-2 (EditPageLink emits no `<title>` element); INV-A11Y-3 (`grep -nE '<h[1-6]' src/components/EditPageLink.astro` → 0 matches; EditPageLink emits zero heading elements — cannot introduce a duplicate H1 or a heading-level skip on any page that renders it); INV-CODE-3 (`grep -nE 'defineCollection|z\.|loader:' src/components/EditPageLink.astro` → 0 matches; no schema-defining calls). DEFERRED — INV-A11Y-1 (`@axe-core/playwright` not yet installed; SG-22 + SG-25 own; iter-17 introduces no axe-flagging patterns — the rendered `<a class="print-hide" href={editUrl} rel="nofollow">Edit this page</a>` is a single text anchor with a descriptive accessible name from its visible text content, which is the simplest accessible-link pattern). BLOCKED — INV-BUILD-2 (`pnpm astro check` requires `@astrojs/check`, not installed; SG-22 owns; no regression from iter-14/15/16 baseline). PARTIAL-CONTRIBUTION — INV-NAV-2 (EditPageLink is not yet rendered in current dist — no layout wraps it; integration is owned by SG-20 — LivingDoc.astro. When integrated, the href resolves through `SOURCE_REPO_URL` which is currently the placeholder `https://github.com/PLACEHOLDER/technodruid` per DECISION-REPO. Phase 4 ISC-P4-REPO-1 + ISC-P4-EDIT-1 own end-to-end edit-URL openability verification. Same forward-coupling pattern as NavBar/SG-14 + index.astro CTAs/SG-21 + Breadcrumbs/SG-15: do not fabricate the integration here, surface the forward-coupling for the integrating subgoal).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Three observations worth recording. (1) **The `<nav>`-as-print-hide pattern from iter-16's reflection is not universal — it has a semantic guardrail.** Iter-16's reflection (3a) proposed wrapping nav-chrome in `<nav>` to inherit print-hiding from global.css:180 for free. SG-16 considered this but rejected: an Edit link is a single utility anchor, not "a set of navigational links" (the W3C ARIA landmark `<nav>` definition at https://www.w3.org/TR/wai-aria-1.2/#navigation). Wrapping a lone `<a>` in `<nav>` purely for the print-suppression side-effect would be semantically dishonest — screen-reader users would hear "navigation, link, Edit this page" where there is no navigation. The cleaner pattern: `<nav>` for true nav (Breadcrumbs, NavBar, page-internal TOC, footer link clusters), `.print-hide` for single utility controls (Edit link, future Comment toggle, future Share controls). Generalizes: optimization for-its-own-sake at the markup level can violate semantic contracts in ways the build doesn't catch; iterate carefully when an iter-N reflection proposes a pattern for iter-N+1. (2) **`rel="nofollow"` on an Edit link is a doctrinal alignment, not an SEO move.** A naive "Edit this page" link would crawl-and-index into the editor's URL space — opening hundreds of `?edit_branch=...&path=...` permutations to search-engine crawlers. `rel="nofollow"` blocks that crawl. This isn't about SEO ranking (which is what most `nofollow` discussions are about) — it's about the IA's archival/discovery doctrine. The Internet Archive is welcome (INV-DOC-5 forbids `noarchive`); search-engine crawlers into write-action URL space are not welcome (no IA invariant covers this, but the doctrine is consistent). Recording for SG-13/SG-14 forward-couplings: if/when Contribute and About pages add similar "open this in the editor" affordances, they should also carry `rel="nofollow"`. Worth considering as a future invariant: `INV-NAV-4 — write-action URLs carry rel="nofollow"`. Not adopted in this iteration — single instance doesn't justify codification. (3) **Defensive prop normalization is the cheapest contract to add early.** Line 9's `sourcePath.replace(/^\/+/, "")` costs almost nothing — one regex operation per render — but eliminates a class of bugs: when SG-20 LivingDoc.astro reaches into a content-collection `entry.id` (Astro v5 convention: leading-slash-free relative path from collection root) versus when a caller hand-passes `"/src/content/living/grove.md"` (leading slash from a copy-paste of a repo-rooted path), the URL output is identical. This is the same defensive pattern as Breadcrumbs.astro:35 `replace(import.meta.env.BASE_URL, "/").replace(/\/+/g, "/")` — normalize at the boundary, not at the caller. Lesson: when a component accepts a string-typed prop that will be joined into a URL, normalize the slash convention inside the component; document the contract through the regex literal, not through JSDoc. Forward-pointers from this iteration: (a) SG-20 LivingDoc.astro should pass `entry.id` to `<EditPageLink sourcePath={entry.id} />` — `entry.id` per Astro v5 content-collection convention is the leading-slash-free relative path, so the `replace` is operationally a no-op for the common case and only activates for accidental leading slashes; (b) when SG-22 lands `@astrojs/check` + the `verify` script chain, the placeholder `SOURCE_REPO_URL = "https://github.com/PLACEHOLDER/technodruid"` will pass type-check (string) but a future Phase 4 link-checker against the placeholder URL will 404 — that's the right time to resolve DECISION-REPO; (c) SG-18 TableOfContents and SG-19 CanonicalDoc + SG-20 LivingDoc all should reconsider iter-16's `<nav>`-as-print-hide pattern per (1) above — wrap only when the element is true navigation; use `.print-hide` for utility chrome.
- **Remaining:** 9 Phase 0 milestones pending (31 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 30 + ISC-FND-CMP-2) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **The `<nav>`-as-print-hide guardrail from iter-17 cuts both ways — it also tells you when *not* to print-hide.** Iter-17's reflection (1) clarified that print-hiding is for editor chrome, not for content. SG-17 took that one step further: VersionFooter is metadata about the document itself (version, amendment date, source-of-record link), so it belongs in the printed archival copy — the version stamp IS the doctrinal claim that "this is version X as of date Y." Printing a canonical document without its version stamp would be like printing a contract without its signature date. Lesson: when iter-N's reflection establishes a categorization (chrome vs nav vs content), iter-N+1 should ask whether the same categorization disambiguates a different choice. Here, "is this chrome or content?" disambiguated "should this be print-hidden?" — VersionFooter is content. (2) **One prop normalization pattern, two consumers — codify before a third arrives.** EditPageLink (SG-16) introduced `sourcePath.replace(/^\/+/, "")`. VersionFooter (SG-17) repeated it verbatim. Both compose URLs of the form `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/<verb>/main/${sourcePath}`. When SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro lands and starts passing `entry.id` (Astro v5 leading-slash-free convention) to both `<EditPageLink>` and `<VersionFooter>`, the regex becomes operationally a no-op for the common case and a defense against accidental leading slashes for edge cases. The rule-of-three for extraction has not been reached (only two callers, both passing what is effectively the same value), so no helper function yet — but it's now worth noting in DECISIONS.md if a third repo-URL-composing component appears, the right move is to extract `function repoUrlFor(verb: 'edit' | 'blob' | 'commits', sourcePath: string): string` in `src/lib/repo.ts` and consume from all three sites. Forward-pointers from iter-18: (a) SG-18 TableOfContents.astro continues the default sequence; it does not consume `SOURCE_REPO_URL`, so the rule-of-three above remains at two consumers; (b) SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro is the integration site for both VersionFooter and TableOfContents — when it lands, the `sourcePath` it passes to `<VersionFooter>` should come from `entry.filePath` or `entry.id` per the Astro v5 content-collection API; (c) when DECISION-REPO resolves, both EditPageLink's `/edit/main/` segment and VersionFooter's `/blob/main/` and `/commits/main/` segments need to be re-checked against the chosen platform's URL grammar — GitHub uses `/edit/<branch>/`, `/blob/<branch>/`, `/commits/<branch>/`; Forgejo uses `/_edit/<branch>/`, `/src/branch/<branch>/`, `/commits/branch/<branch>/`. A platform switch is a non-trivial edit across at least these two files and ideally the extracted `repoUrlFor` helper noted above.
- **Remaining:** 8 Phase 0 milestones pending (32 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 31 + ISC-FND-CMP-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-CMP-5 (three independent sub-checks against PRD line 244 spec: (1) `headings: MarkdownHeading[]` prop accepted — line 2 `import type { MarkdownHeading } from "astro"` resolves to `@astrojs/markdown-remark@6.3.9/dist/types.d.ts:70-74` (`{depth:number; slug:string; text:string}`); line 5 `headings: MarkdownHeading[];` inside `interface Props`; line 8 destructures from `Astro.props`. (2) Sticky — line 14 `class="sticky top-4 text-sm"` on the `<nav>` element; `sticky` Tailwind utility maps to `position: sticky` per Tailwind v4 default theme. (3) Scroll-spy — lines 29-58 inline `<script>`: `IntersectionObserver` instantiated at line 44 with `rootMargin '0px 0px -75% 0px'` (top-quarter activation, prevents flicker when multiple headings briefly cross the viewport bottom); on intersection lines 46-54 it clears `aria-current` from all links then sets `aria-current="true"` on the link whose `data-toc-link` slug matches the intersecting heading's `id` (Astro auto-slugs headings to element ids matching `MarkdownHeading.slug`). (4) `depth <= 3` — line 9 `const items = headings.filter((h) => h.depth <= 3);` filters in-spec; line 18 `h.depth === 3 && "pl-4"` indents depth-3 entries for visual hierarchy. Build PASS proves Astro compiled the component).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **Case-sensitive invariant greps are a verification-liability when the asserted text and the implementation diverge in casing.** Iter-19's first attempt at INV-NAV-1's grep returned 0 matches against NavBar.astro and briefly looked like a real regression — but NavBar uses uppercase labels (`CREED`, `CODEX`, …) as a CRT-aesthetic convention, while `docs/invariant_requirements.md:151` lists them in title case ("Creed, Codex, Practices…"). The text content renders identically (browsers do not normalize), the doctrinal requirement (six entries in IA §4 order, no extras) is met, and the case-insensitive re-run confirmed PASS. Lesson for SG-24 `tests/invariants.spec.ts`: NavBar-presence-and-order assertions should be case-insensitive (the invariant is *which entries appear in what order*, not the literal casing of the source) AND should require ALL six labels in order, not just any. A future invariant could codify casing if that becomes load-bearing, but it is not load-bearing today. (2) **The TOC integration with SG-19 has a correct-by-construction guarantee worth preserving in the CanonicalDoc wiring.** Because the heading list (rendered into the page) and the TOC link list both come from the same `MarkdownHeading[]` returned by Astro's content-collection `render()` call, the `#${slug}` fragments cannot drift from the heading `id`s. When SG-19 lands, the wiring should pass `entry.headings` directly to `<TableOfContents>` without intermediate transformation — any transform (re-slugging, filtering by section, depth-clipping above what's already in this component) introduces a divergence opportunity that the build-time link checker (SG-26) would catch only after the fact. This is a strictly stronger guarantee than the build-time link checker SG-26 will provide for cross-page links, and is worth a one-line comment in CanonicalDoc.astro when written. Forward-pointers from iter-19: (a) SG-19 CanonicalDoc.astro consumes both VersionFooter (SG-17) and TableOfContents (this iteration), so it is the natural integration boundary — pass `entry.headings` to `<TableOfContents>` and `entry.id` (Astro v5 leading-slash-free) plus `entry.data.{version,amendedAt,firstPublishedAt}` to `<VersionFooter>`; (b) iter-18 reflection (2)'s `repoUrlFor` extraction trigger remains at two consumers (EditPageLink + VersionFooter); TableOfContents introduces no third consumer; (c) the inline IntersectionObserver pattern in TableOfContents.astro:29-58 is the first inline `<script>` in a Phase 0 component — if subsequent components need similar progressive-enhancement JS (e.g., a future copy-to-clipboard for canonical text, or a print-friendly toggle), DECISIONS.md should record whether to keep them inline per-component (locality, no bundling overhead) or extract to `src/scripts/` (reuse, hoisting, but adds an import indirection). For one occurrence, inline is correct; for three or more, extract.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **Extending a load-bearing root layout safely means making the default a no-op.** Base.astro is consumed by every page in the site, today and forever, so any prop addition must not change the rendered HTML for existing callers. The chosen pattern — `["flex", "items-center", bodyClass].filter(Boolean).join(" ")` with `bodyClass?: string` defaulting to `undefined` — is bit-identical for existing index.astro (the filter drops the undefined, producing exactly `"flex items-center"`). Verification: dist/index.html before and after this iteration should differ by zero bytes inside the `<body>` tag. The lesson generalizes: when adding an optional prop to a shared root, the falsy/undefined path must produce exactly the prior output. A naive implementation like `<body class={\`flex items-center ${bodyClass ?? ""}\`}>` would introduce a trailing space — visually invisible but bit-different — and a brittle test could regress on it. The `filter(Boolean).join(" ")` idiom is the safer composition. Worth codifying in DECISIONS.md if a third layout extends Base with a similar opt-in class — at that point an `assembleBodyClasses(...parts: (string | undefined)[]): string` helper in `src/lib/css.ts` may earn its keep. (2) **`entry.filePath` is the correct sourcePath provenance in Astro v5, but the fallback chain matters.** Astro v5's content-collection entry exposes `filePath` as a string like `"./src/content/canonical/codex.md"` (per Astro v5 docs); my implementation defensively chains `entry.filePath ?? "src/content/canonical/${entry.id}"` with a `.replace(/^\.\//, "")` to strip the leading `./` that Astro adds. This handles three failure modes simultaneously: (a) Astro v5 surface drift where `filePath` becomes optional — fallback to `entry.id`; (b) accidental Astro internals that strip `filePath` — same fallback; (c) the standard case where `filePath` is the documented `"./src/..."` — strip the `./` so the joined URL never produces `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/blob/main/./src/...`. The chain is three lines of defensive logic that buy resilience across a real Astro version change. Forward-pointers from iter-20: (a) SG-20 LivingDoc.astro should mirror this pattern — accept `entry: CollectionEntry<"living">`, compute sourcePath the same way for EditPageLink, but living entries also need lastEditedAt + contributors which come from `entry.data` (lastEditedAt, contributors) per content.config.ts:21-24; (b) SG-21 index.astro was already pulled forward in iter-15; SG-19's CanonicalDoc landing now enables Phase 1 ISC-MVP-4 (codex page) to start using `<CanonicalDoc entry={entry} headings={headings}><Content /></CanonicalDoc>` once a canonical entry exists; (c) the rule-of-three for `repoUrlFor` extraction remains at two consumers (EditPageLink + VersionFooter) — CanonicalDoc composes through VersionFooter rather than introducing a third direct composer, so the helper is still deferred; SG-20 LivingDoc will also compose through EditPageLink rather than directly, preserving the two-consumer count; (d) iter-19 reflection (1)'s case-insensitive grep convention applied successfully this iteration without any false-negative scare — the convention should become permanent in SG-24 invariants.spec.ts; (e) the optional-prop-default-no-op pattern from reflection (1) should be invoked verbatim when SG-22 lands and the `verify` script chain runs — any future Base.astro prop addition (e.g., `noindex?: boolean` for `/about/contact` if it ever needs robot exclusion) should be code-reviewed against the bit-identical-when-default heuristic.
- **Remaining:** 6 Phase 0 milestones pending (34 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 33 + ISC-FND-LAY-1) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

Direct ISC PASS — ISC-FND-LAY-2 (eight-point sub-check against PRD line 239 spec: (1) `entry: CollectionEntry<"living">` accepted — LivingDoc.astro:10 typed in Props interface, :13 destructured from Astro.props; (2) `<Breadcrumbs>` rendered — line 21; (3) `<LivingBadge>` rendered — line 23 (wrapped in `<div class="mt-4">` for spacing without inline-style); (4) `<h1>` from title — line 25 `<h1>{title}</h1>`; (5) slotted MDX content — line 26 `<slot />`; (6) `<LastEditedStamp>` — line 28 receives `date={lastEditedAt}` destructured from `entry.data` at line 14; (7) contributor list — line 29 `<p>Contributors: {contributorList}</p>`; `contributorList` computed at line 16 from `entry.data.contributors` (string[], default [] per content.config.ts:23) with empty-array fallback to "—"; (8) `<EditPageLink>` resolving to entry's source path — line 31 receives sourcePath computed at line 15 with three-tier provenance: `entry.data.sourcePath` (schema-declared optional override per content.config.ts:24) → `entry.filePath` (Astro v5 documented field) → `"src/content/living/${entry.id}"` (constructed fallback); `.replace(/^\.\//, "")` strips Astro's documented `./` prefix so the joined URL never produces `${SOURCE_REPO_URL}/edit/main/./src/...`).
- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Two observations. (1) **An optional schema field becomes a deliberate override only when the layout's provenance chain prefers it over the structural default.** The living schema's `sourcePath: z.string().optional()` field would be dead weight if the layout used `entry.filePath` unconditionally. The three-tier chain `entry.data.sourcePath ?? entry.filePath ?? constructed-fallback` gives the schema field a real purpose — an author who needs to point "Edit this page" at a different repo path (e.g., living content sourced from a Wiki module, a fork, or an alternate branch) can set it via frontmatter without touching the layout. CanonicalDoc deliberately omits this tier because canonical content has no equivalent schema override (canonical schema lists no `sourcePath`). The lesson: don't shrug at "optional" schema fields — either delete them (if no layout consumes them) or wire them through the provenance chain (if they're meant to override defaults). Forward-pointer for SG-6 caretaker: if `living.sourcePath` is never used in practice, it should be removed in a content-config cleanup pass; the cost of carrying an unused optional field is documentation drift, not bytes. (2) **Invariant-by-fallback is stronger than invariant-by-discipline when the schema allows the failure mode.** INV-LIV-1 mandates "contributor list (may be a single entry)." The schema permits `contributors: []` via `.default([])`. If the layout renders nothing when the array is empty, the invariant fails for entries that ship with an empty contributors list — and the failure is a content bug, surfaced only by tests against actual pages. The `contributors.length > 0 ? contributors.join(", ") : "—"` fallback at line 16 shifts the guarantee from author discipline (must remember to add contributors) to layout structural enforcement (the "Contributors:" line is always present, even if its value is the em-dash placeholder). The trade-off: an "empty contributors" page now reads "Contributors: —" instead of being structurally invalid — visible to the reader as a marker that the field exists but is unfilled. For a doctrinally-archival site, visible-absent is better than silently-absent. Forward-pointers from iter-21: (a) SG-20 closes the layout-component layer (Base + CanonicalDoc + LivingDoc) — Phase 0 milestones remaining are testing infrastructure (SG-22 package.json deps + scripts, SG-23 playwright config, SG-24 invariants spec, SG-25 a11y spec, SG-26 build spec); (b) the natural next subgoal is SG-22 (package.json), because it unblocks `pnpm astro check` (INV-BUILD-2), `pnpm test` (SG-23..26), and the `verify` script chain — every subsequent test subgoal depends on it; (c) iter-10 forward-pointer for SG-22 still live: DECIDE whether `verify` runs greenfield (asserts full chain passes) or progressively (scripts exist, baseline failures accepted); given INV-BUILD-1 PASS for 7 consecutive iterations (iter-15..21) and no canonical/living pages yet, greenfield is now achievable for the check + build halves but not test:ci (no tests exist yet — chicken-and-egg); the resolution is staged: install deps + add scripts in SG-22, accept that `test:ci` will exit non-zero until SG-23/24 exist, then re-verify after each test file lands; (d) iter-19 reflection (1) case-insensitive invariant grep convention has held for two iterations (iter-20, iter-21) — codify in SG-24 invariants.spec.ts when written; (e) the `repoUrlFor` rule-of-three remains at two consumers (EditPageLink, VersionFooter); LivingDoc composes through EditPageLink rather than introducing a third direct composer — pattern from iter-20 reflection (1) preserved; first real third-consumer trigger likely lands in Phase 2 (e.g., wheel-events RSS feed item permalinks referencing repo paths, ISC-P2-6).
- **Remaining:** 5 Phase 0 milestones pending (35 of 40 satisfied: previously satisfied 34 + ISC-FND-LAY-2) + Phase 1/2/3/4 ISCs not yet decomposed.

- **Overall:** PASS
- **Reflection:** Three observations. (1) **A 4-iteration BLOCKED invariant is not a stall — it's a deferred dependency.** INV-BUILD-2 was BLOCKED for iter-18/19/20/21 because `@astrojs/check` was not installed; the loop kept marking it BLOCKED rather than treating BLOCKED as FAIL. This is a deliberate design feature: invariants whose toolchain isn't installed yet cannot regress the iteration, and the right resolution is to land the unlock subgoal (here, SG-22) before any subgoal that would re-encounter the missing toolchain. The lesson: when classifying an invariant as BLOCKED, the loop owes a forward-pointer to the unblocking subgoal — and that subgoal's pre-flight must include the unblocked invariant explicitly so the unblocking is verified, not implied. SG-22's pre-flight did this for INV-BUILD-2: PASS with explicit BLOCKED→PASS transition evidence. (2) **Script EXISTENCE vs script PASSING is a contract distinction worth honoring.** PRD line 213 says `package.json includes ... scripts test, test:ci, check, verify (where verify chains check → build → test:ci)`. It does NOT say `pnpm verify exits 0`. Iter-22 honored the literal contract: scripts exist and chain correctly (verified via `jq '.scripts.verify | test("check[^&]*&&[^&]*build[^&]*&&[^&]*test:ci")'` → true), but `pnpm verify` itself was not executed because `test:ci` would exit non-zero pre-SG-23/24 (no Playwright tests yet — chicken-and-egg). The staged-resolution from iter-21 forward-pointer (c) was applied: install + wire in SG-22, accept `test:ci` non-zero, re-verify after SG-23/24/25/26 land. Without this distinction, SG-22 would be unsolvable without merging in SG-23/24 — violating the loop's "one iteration unit per iteration" rule. Forward-pointer: when SG-26 lands the last test file, run `pnpm verify` end-to-end and capture EXIT=0 as the proof-of-chain evidence; that becomes the first true greenfield verify pass. (3) **`pnpm add -D` is the correct tool for SG-22 — not direct package.json edits — because lockfile atomicity matters.** Editing `package.json`'s `devDependencies` and then running `pnpm install` is a two-step that can leave `pnpm-lock.yaml` momentarily inconsistent if the install fails (e.g., network blip, registry rate limit). `pnpm add -D pkg1 pkg2 pkg3` atomically writes both files. The "Ignored build scripts: esbuild, sharp" warning is benign — those are postinstall opt-ins (pnpm 10+ security feature), and the 8-iter INV-BUILD-1 green streak proves the binaries already work from prior approval. Recommendation for future infra subgoals: prefer `pnpm add -D` over manual JSON edits for any dependency change. Forward-pointers from iter-22: (a) **new SG-27 (cleanup) candidate** — delete `src/components/HeroImage.astro` (orphan, INV-CODE-2 violator) AND `src/assets/blog-fallback.jpg` (orphan from SG-11 forward-pointer); single trivial iteration closes two carryovers; ORIENT step 4b should add this in iter-23 if no PRD changes intervene. (b) **SG-23 (`tests/playwright.config.ts`) is the natural next subgoal** — it's standard tier, depends on `@playwright/test` (now installed), and unlocks SG-24/25/26. The config should set `webServer: { command: 'pnpm preview', url: 'http://localhost:4321', reuseExistingServer: !process.env.CI }` per PRD line 318-style spec; testDir likely `./tests`. (c) **iter-21 reflection (1)'s schema-field-deletion forward-pointer for `living.sourcePath`** remains live — should fold into SG-27 cleanup or a follow-on once a real living entry exists to test against. (d) **codify the `jq`-for-JSON convention** for future loop verifications — `jq` was used here per `feedback_jq_for_json` memory, and `jq -r '.scripts.verify | test("...")'` proved cleaner than `node -e` for the chain-regex assertion. (e) **case-insensitive grep convention** held for three consecutive iterations (iter-20, iter-21, iter-22) — codify in SG-24 `invariants.spec.ts` as a hard rule, not a soft preference.
